He pays off the Champions' outstanding LA liabilities personally and quietly; receipts implied across *Defenders* #62–65, where he resurfaces with Iceman in a different team without ever mentioning the previous one.
- **Bobby Drake** follows Warren almost without volition — the *attachment trail* is observable: when Warren goes east, Bobby goes east. He never lives in Los Angeles again. His Champions period is *never* referenced as formative in his own subsequent voice; in *X-Factor* (1986–) and through every Iceman solo to the present, the team is conspicuous by its absence from his memory inventory.
- **Natasha Romanoff** vanishes back into espionage geography. By *Daredevil* #155 she is in New York; thereafter SHIELD, KGB-cleanup, Champions-of-the-Self era. She will not publicly affiliate with a fixed-roster super-team for nearly a decade.
- **Johnny Blaze** drives. Literally. The post-Champions Ghost Rider issues (*Ghost Rider* vol. 2, mid-50s onward) are a road book — Blaze leaves Los Angeles on the bike and is essentially never tied to a fixed address again until the late 1990s. The Champions chapter is excised from his self-narrative so completely that even his later confessional arcs (the Caretaker years, the Hell-on-Earth arc) skip it entirely.
- **Hercules** returns to Olympus, then is exiled again, then joins the Avengers (*Avengers* #163 onward). The Champions are, to Hercules's bardic self-mythology, *the chapter not sung*. His drinking-song catalog name-checks every battle from Troy to Ultron; the LA team is not in the cycle.

**Diagnostic note.** The post-dissolution period is when a healthy team's *alumni network* forms — birthday calls, ad-hoc reunions, the persistence of the "we" in private. The Champions generate **none** of this. By 1982 the five members have, between them, fewer cross-references in dialogue than any other co-served Marvel roster of comparable duration. The silence is the data.

---

## B. The Long Silence (1982–2000): Active Disavowal as Maintenance Behavior

For approximately eighteen real-time years, the original Champions roster operates as a *negative space* in Marvel continuity. The team is referenced almost exclusively in:

1. **Self-deprecating beats by Warren Worthington III.** In *X-Factor* (Louise Simonson run) and the early Peter David *X-Factor*, Warren has a recurring habit of waving off the Champions period when it comes up — usually with phrasing that codes embarrassment as wry distance. He is the only member who *acknowledges* the team, and his acknowledgment is uniformly apologetic.
2. **Continuity-housekeeping by editors.** Handbook entries, *Marvel Saga*, the occasional footnote. These are bureaucratic, not narrative.
3. **Brief nostalgic cameos in retrospectives** (*Avengers Forever*, *Marvel Universe*, *Marvels*-adjacent material). The team appears in group-photo composites and flashback panels. They are never *spoken about* by other characters in these appearances. They are *seen* and not *discussed*.

**The active disavowal pattern.** This is not mere forgetting; it is a maintenance behavior. Each member, when in proximity to a former teammate in another title, exhibits a recognizable micro-avoidance:

- **Warren + Bobby** (continuously co-served in X-titles): the Champions are never invoked between them on-panel during the entire Simonson, early Peter David, or Mutant Massacre/Inferno periods. Two men who lived in the same Los Angeles house for two years and bled together against the Stranger, and the subject does not come up. This is not editorial oversight — it is *characterological*. They have agreed, somatically, not to revisit.
- **Warren + Natasha** (cross paths in *Avengers* and *Uncanny X-Men* crossovers): cordial, professional, structurally distant. No "remember when" register is ever activated.
- **Natasha + Hercules** (both Avengers reservists at various points): they served on the same team. They do not, on-panel, ever discuss it. Their Avengers-era interactions are first-meeting in affect.
- **Blaze, with anyone:** the Ghost Rider title's editorial culture in this era is hermetically sealed; he meets X-Men, Avengers, and Punisher characters in his own book and the Champions are never raised, by him or by them.

**Clinical interpretation.** This collective behavior is consistent with **shared shame-management**: a group that does not name a chapter because naming it would force a reckoning none of the parties has the bandwidth for. It is also consistent with **avoidant attachment in long maintenance**: the loss was never grieved, so the topic remains affectively hot, so the topic remains untouched.

---

## C. The Name Reuses (2003–Present): The Trademark Lives, The Team Doesn't

The Champions *name* has been resurrected three times in the modern era. **In none of these revivals is the original team re-formed, re-convened, or even meaningfully consulted.**

1. **Champions, Inc. (2007, Zeb Wells / Sean Chen, 5-issue limited).** A Los Angeles-based super-team led by the Hank Pym Ant-Man, with Darkstar, Gravity, and others — a deliberate evocation of the LA mandate, geographically faithful, rosterwise unrelated. Warren Worthington's company is invoked obliquely as a trademark-holding entity; this is the **first canonical confirmation** that the Champions IP was retained by Worthington Industries after dissolution. **Inference:** Warren never let the name go. He paid the lawyers to keep it on the shelf. That is not the behavior of a man who is over it.
2. **Champions (2016–2019, Mark Waid / Humberto Ramos; relaunched several times since).** The teen team — Ms. Marvel, Nova, Miles Morales, Viv Vision, Amadeus Cho, Cyclops (time-displaced) — explicitly takes the name as an *aspirational* banner, treating the original LA Champions as a *historical reference point*, an idea worth recovering. The original members are never consulted on-panel. Warren signs paperwork off-panel granting use of the name (referenced obliquely in editorial material). **Inference:** Warren views the trademark as redeemable in *other* hands more easily than his own.
3. **Scattered "Champions of Los Angeles" cameos** in *Avengers* and *X-Men* flashback issues, *Hawkeye: Freefall*, *Strikeforce*, and ancillary material. The team is now a recognized historical formation — a *thing that happened* — and writers can deploy it as shorthand for "1970s West Coast hero culture." It functions as period set-dressing, not as living continuity.

**Pattern across reuses:** the name is more usable than the team. The Champions brand has a half-life longer than the unit's affective life by a factor of three.

---

## D. Current Status of the Formation (Present)

**Operational status of the original Champions of Los Angeles as a team: dormant. No reunion ever convened. No protocol exists for convening one.** The five-member field roster has not been in the same physical room, on-panel, since *Champions* #17. Brief two- and three-member convergences have occurred incidentally (Warren-Bobby continuously; Natasha-Hercules in Avengers contexts; Blaze with various of them in event books like *Secret Wars*, *Civil War II*, *War of the Realms*), but **a full five-way reconvening has not happened in nearly five decades of publication time.**

This is, statistically, remarkable. Every other Marvel super-team of comparable vintage — the original X-Men, the founding Avengers, the Fantastic Four, the Defenders, the Inhumans, the Invaders — has reconvened in original-roster form at least once, usually multiple times, for anniversaries, events, or nostalgic miniseries. The Champions, alone, have not. **Editorial does not propose it; the surviving members would not, in their current characterizations, agree to it.**

### Current member status (as of present-tense continuity, late 2010s–2020s span):

- **Warren Worthington III.** Has cycled through Angel, Archangel, Death-of-the-Horsemen, Apocalypse-influenced regressions, and the Krakoan-era resurrection economy. Currently on Krakoa / post-Krakoa X-roster, serving as one of the X-Men's institutional pillars and intermittent financial backbone. **Champions residue:** the trademark, the embarrassment, the unspoken sense that the team was *his* failed project. He is the only member who carries it as personal liability rather than impersonal episode. In private moments across recent X-titles, when Champions-era characters surface (Darkstar most notably), his affect goes briefly flat — a tell of unresolved material.
- **Bobby Drake.** Out, on the X-Men, far more powerful than his Champions-era output suggested. His Omega-level capability development happened entirely *after* the Champions, and he has, in late-period self-narration, treated the LA period as the *immaturity baseline* against which his subsequent growth is measured. He doesn't talk about the Champions because the Champions were Bobby-before-Bobby-was-Bobby. **Residue:** developmental, formative-by-negation, not affectively hot but quietly present in his comparative self-assessment.
- **Natasha Romanoff.** Has died and returned (the LMD arc, the Tony Stark resurrection in *Black Widow* (2019 Soule), the subsequent Kelly Thompson run, the Bucky-coded recent appearances). Has been Avengers chair, SHIELD director-equivalent, KGB-cleanup czar, and solo operator. **Champions residue:** functionally none in her on-panel biography. She has been *killed and resurrected* and the LA chapter still does not surface in her reconstituted memory inventory. This is either deepest avoidance or the cleanest excision in the file — most likely both. If asked directly, in current characterization, she would describe the period as "a wilderness year between Matt and the next thing." That phrasing would be true and would also be a containment strategy.
- **Johnny Blaze.** Has been *King of Hell*, has lost the King of Hell title, has been split from and reconciled with Danny Ketch, has been driven through multiple Damnation/Avengers-of-the-Supernatural arcs (*Damnation*, *Avengers* Aaron run, *Ghost Rider* Percy/Howard runs). He is, somatically, in his most unstable phase since the original Zarathos era. **Champions residue:** the *containment failure* prediction (pressure point #5 in the prior synthesis) has been borne out, repeatedly, in his post-Champions life — every uncontrolled Rider episode he has had in the last twenty years is a delayed instance of the protocol gap the Champions never built. He has never reflected on this connection. He may not be capable of doing so.
- **Hercules.** Has died (the Chaos War arc), returned, lost and recovered divinity, run for a season as a street-level New York hero in the Pak/Van Lente *Herc* solo, rejoined Avengers iterations, served in the *Guardians of the Galaxy* / cosmic register. **Champions residue:** zero on-panel. His bardic catalog still does not include the LA team. When pressed by interlocutors in the Pak/Van Lente run about his myriad past affiliations, the Champions are skipped over. **Inference:** for Hercules, the team registers as *not-myth-worthy* — too brief, too inglorious, too non-Olympian in stakes. The cataloging silence is itself a form of judgment.

### The supporting cast, current status (briefly):

- **Darkstar (Laynia Petrovna).** Killed in the Children of the Vault arc, resurrected via Krakoan protocols, currently on the Russian-mutant orbit. She is the **only** surviving regular from the Champions supporting cast who carries the LA period as positive memory; her brief Champions-era was, for her, a defection arc that succeeded. She would attend a reunion. No one is calling her.
- **Rampage (Stuart Clarke).** Has cycled in and out as a D-list villain and intermittent reformee. He remains, in absentia, the team's unmetabolized critique — the proof that the mandate failed its first test case. The Champions have never circled back to *resolve* him.
- **Black Goliath, the Stranger, the Griffin, Swarm, MODOK** — all dispersed into general Marvel continuity, none meaningfully tied back to the LA period.

---

## E. The Counterfactual That Did Not Happen

In a healthy team-life arc, the Champions would have reconvened — once, in the late 1990s or early 2000s, probably under a *Marvel Knights* or *Marvel Team-Up* banner, probably for a one-shot or limited that allowed the five surviving members to grieve, to name what happened, and to either re-form or formally part. **This reunion has not occurred and shows no editorial signs of occurring.** Every other comparable team has had its version of this issue; the Champions have not.

The reasons, derived from the behavioral record:

1. **No member has standing to call it.** Warren is the only one with both the resources and the residual investment, and Warren's own affect around the period (embarrassment, financial-residue ownership) makes him the *least* likely to convene it. The man who paid for the headquarters is the man who cannot bear to walk back into the room.
2. **No external pressure compels it.** The Champions never made an enemy who survives at a tier high enough to require five-member response. There is no *return-of-the-Stranger* event waiting; the franchise's threat-pipeline has moved on without them.
3. **The surviving members' current ensembles absorb their bandwidth.** Warren on X-Men, Bobby on X-Men, Natasha on Avengers/solo, Hercules on Avengers/cosmic, Blaze on Ghost Rider/Damnation. Each is, in modern continuity, *over-rostered*. There is no calendar space for a Champions reunion even if anyone wanted one.
4. **The shame-management equilibrium is stable.** Forty-five-plus years of not-talking-about-it has become its own institution. Breaking it would require an act of will none of the five characters, as currently written, possesses with respect to this specific subject.

---

## F. Current-State Synthesis

**The Champions of Los Angeles exist, in the present continuity, as a perfectly preserved fossil.** The formation has not been reanimated and will not be, not because it is forgotten but because it is *load-bearing in its absence*. Each surviving member's current self-construction relies, quietly, on the Champions chapter remaining closed. Warren needs it to stay closed to maintain his self-image as a serious institutional X-Men figure rather than a man who once funded a vanity project; Bobby needs it closed to maintain his Omega-era self-account; Natasha needs it closed to maintain the clean lines of her espionage biography; Hercules needs it closed to maintain the integrity of his bardic catalog; Blaze needs it closed because opening it would require examining a Rider-containment failure pattern he is still actively living inside.

**The team's current state is therefore best described as: dormant by mutual unspoken agreement, preserved by trademark, embarrassed in retrospect, and structurally unreconvenable.** The name lives on a younger team's chest. The infrastructure was liquidated decades ago. The five bodies that once shared a polyglot ER without a triage nurse have dispersed into five separate trauma-and-glory arcs, each of which has, in its own way, outgrown the LA period and refused to outgrow the silence around it.

**The dossier's terminal observation:** a team that ends without a funeral does not, ever, fully end. The Champions are not over. They are *suspended* — held in the unspoken contract among five people that this thing happened, and that none of them will be the one to bring it up. That contract, observed over four-plus decades of publication, is the most coherent collective behavior the Champions have ever produced. They could not agree on a mission statement, a chain of command, a moral framework, or a dissolution protocol. They agreed, perfectly and without speaking, never to come back.

That is, in its own way, the most successful piece of teamwork in the file.

— UATU, observing the silence.


## Medical History

# MEDICAL HISTORY — THE CHAMPIONS (Los Angeles, Original Roster)

*A composite somatic file for a five-body unit. The team has no single physiology; it has a five-channel medical record that must be read in parallel and across the run, because the team's tactical decisions, social pathology, and ultimate dissolution are downstream of facts that any competent unit-surgeon would have flagged on intake.*

---

## 1. INTAKE PHYSICALS (October 1975, in-universe; *Champions* #1)

No intake physicals were performed. The team did not pass through a medical gate of any kind at formation. There is no record of baseline vitals, no blood draw, no allergy panel, no neurological screen, no psychiatric intake, no informed-consent documentation regarding mission risk. The Avengers, the Fantastic Four, S.H.I.E.L.D., even the Defenders' informal mutual referrals through Strange's Sanctum, all have at minimum an examining physician of record. The Champions have none. This is the foundational medical fact of the unit: **the team operates for its entire run without a medical officer, a designated trauma facility, a stocked infirmary beyond a domestic first-aid level, or any standing relationship with a hospital that knows what it is receiving.** Warren's wealth could have bought all of this in a weekend. It did not occur to anyone to ask.

The downstream consequence is that every entry below is reconstructed from incidents, not from records. The team's medical history is its battle log, and that is itself the diagnosis.

---

## 2. HERCULES — OLYMPIAN PHYSIOLOGY, CHRONIC INTOXICATION

**Baseline.** Class-100 strength tier; demigod-to-god metabolism; effective immortality; pain threshold orders of magnitude above human; bone density and dermal integrity such that small-arms fire is a tactile annoyance. Healing factor sufficient to close lacerations on a panel-to-panel timescale. He cannot be triaged by human protocols and will not present symptoms in a way ER staff could read.

**Injury record across the run.** Direct blows from Typhon (sustained, retaliatory, mythic-tier); energy assault from Pluto's retinue; the Stranger's manipulations (less an injury than a metaphysical insult to a being who experiences metaphysical insults as injuries); concussive damage from Sentinel weaponry in the terminal arc. None of these required intervention. Hercules walks them off — literally, often to a bar. The team learns by repetition that *Hercules does not need help*, and this learned non-response generalizes catastrophically to bodies that do.

**Chronic alcohol use.** The single most consequential entry in the entire team medical file. Hercules's wine consumption is canonical, daily, often pre-combat. Played in panel as comic; read clinically, it is a sustained, high-volume intake pattern that for any non-Olympian would constitute severe alcohol use disorder. Olympian metabolism processes ethanol on a curve mortal medicine cannot model, but **behavioral disinhibition is observable**: he challenges, boasts, drinks more, fights more. The team's permissive stance — no one ever asks him to be sober for a briefing, no one ever flags it — establishes a unit-wide norm that **intoxication is acceptable on duty**, which then licenses softer versions of the same in others (Blaze's isolation drinking, Romanoff's deliberate use of alcohol as a social anaesthetic).

**Psychological impact.** Hercules's invulnerability is the team's secret psychological permission slip to be reckless. If the strongest member cannot be hurt, the team underestimates the cost of contact for the rest. Hercules himself experiences the run as **a manageable exile from Olympus, lubricated**: there is no on-panel evidence he registers the Champions as a meaningful attachment, which is consistent with a being for whom mortal-timescale relationships are weather.

---

## 3. NATASHA ROMANOFF — TRAUMA SUBSTRATE, PHARMACOLOGICAL HISTORY, FIELD ATHLETICISM

**Baseline.** Peak-human female, conditioned to an upper-elite intelligence-operator standard. Augmented longevity via the Red Room's variant of the Soviet super-soldier program (the full extent of which was not publicly cataloged in 1975 but was, by Romanoff's own self-knowledge, in her body). No superhuman strength, no superhuman durability. She is the most fragile load-bearing member of the team and the most experienced casualty.

**Surgical and pharmacological history (pre-Champions, carried in).** Red Room enhancement protocols — by canon disclosed across her later titles, but operationally present in her body at Champions intake — include cellular conditioning, lifespan extension, false memory implantation, and conditioning regimens whose pharmacology she cannot fully account for. She arrives with a body that has been *previously modified by an adversary*, an exposure profile no teammate is briefed on. She also carries the residue of the synthetic adrenal compounds and reflex-enhancers used in her KGB and post-defection career.

**Injury record across the run.** Concussive injuries (multiple); a notable knife wound during the Griffin engagement; soft-tissue damage from energy weapons in the Sentinel arc; cumulative micro-trauma to wrists, shoulders, and knees consistent with a fighter operating at her output without scheduled physiotherapy. She self-treats. There is no record of her being seen by a physician during the Champions period.

**Substance.** Functional alcohol use, social and self-regulatory. Stimulant use consistent with operator practice, undisclosed to team. Sleep architecture chronically disrupted — the run shows her active at all hours, which is in-character but is, medically, a sleep-deprivation pattern that degrades the very judgment she is elected to provide.

**Psychological impact.** Romanoff's body carries the most untreated material on the team. She is the only member with the training to recognize this and the only member whose training also instructs her **not to disclose it**. The result is a leadership-tier operator running a team while concealing her own medical and psychological substrate from people whose lives depend on knowing it. The recent rupture with Murdock has not been processed; it presents somatically as the hyper-tasking and emotional flatness observable in the Englehart issues. She is, on intake, an undiagnosed complex-PTSD presentation in a unit with no clinician.

---

## 4. JOHNNY BLAZE — METAPHYSICAL POSSESSION, UNTREATED

**Baseline.** Human male, late twenties, professional stunt rider — meaning baseline-human-plus in conditioning, reflex, pain tolerance, and orthopedic resilience, with the specific occupational injury profile of a motorcycle daredevil (healed fractures of clavicle, ribs, scaphoid; chronic lumbar; burn scars from stunt work pre-dating the Zarathos bonding).

**The condition.** Fused with the demonic entity Zarathos via the soul-pact that opens his solo title. Transformation to the Ghost Rider state is **involuntary, externally cued (darkness, threat, the presence of evil), and not under reliable conscious control**. In the transformed state his body is replaced by a hellfire-suffused, skeletal form with weapons, mobility, and damage outputs that bear no relation to his baseline physiology. Reversion is equally uncontrolled. He does not remember all of what Zarathos does while in possession.

**This is, in any honest clinical reading, a chronic dissociative condition with a supernatural etiology** — a body that is repeatedly displaced by another consciousness, with amnestic gaps, ego-dystonic actions performed in the alternate state, and no pharmacological or behavioral protocol for management. The Champions integrate him into the duty roster with no containment plan, no safe-room, no sober second on standby. They treat the possession as a power. It is a power; it is also a crisis condition the unit is unequipped to hold.

**Injury record.** In the Blaze body: motorcycle-related trauma from in-character stunt sequences; concussive injury in the Pluto engagement; burns (paradoxically, given his transformed state's pyrokinesis); cumulative repetitive strain. In the Ghost Rider body: structurally non-applicable — the form regenerates as fast as it is damaged within the run.

**Substance.** Light. Isolation drinking pattern when off-mission, consistent with the affective profile of a man who experiences his own body as occupied territory.

**Psychological impact.** Blaze's medical situation is the team's largest unspoken liability. He knows it. The others do not want to know it. The mandate of "for the common man" is *most fragile here*: a single uncontained Zarathos episode in a civilian context would invalidate the entire premise of the team's existence, and there is no protocol because there is no honest conversation. He sits on the roster like an unexploded ordnance everyone has decided to call a teammate.

---

## 5. WARREN WORTHINGTON III — MUTANT FLIGHT METABOLISM, ORTHOPEDIC LIABILITY

**Baseline.** Mutant, late adolescence to early twenties during the Champions run. Hollow-boned skeletal architecture (avian convergence), elevated metabolic rate, functional wings with a wingspan in the sixteen-foot range, flight ceiling and endurance well in excess of unassisted human capability but well short of, e.g., the Avenging Host tier. Standard X-Men training in hand-to-hand and tactical flight.

**Caloric and recovery profile.** A flight-capable human metabolism requires intake and recovery the team does not schedule. Warren eats more than the others by a wide margin and the team treats this as a quirk rather than a medical fact. Sleep needs are elevated; he is the member most often visibly fatigued in late-issue panels.

**Hollow-bone fragility.** This is the chronic medical truth of his body and the entire team forgets it. The wings articulate at the shoulder via a skeletal architecture that is *light because it is fragile*. He is the team member most easily and most catastrophically maimable. The Sentinel arc's aerial sequences put him at risk repeatedly without compensation. The subsequent canonical maiming of his wings in *X-Factor* / *The Fall of the Mutants* is foreshadowed by the Champions period's casual disregard for the orthopedic stakes of putting Warren in air-to-air against weapons designed to mutate-hunt.

**Injury record across the run.** Wing-membrane lacerations (multiple, self-treated); shoulder strain consistent with carrying teammates in flight without harness; concussive injuries from aerial collisions; burns to the underside of the wings from energy weapons. He never sees a sports-medicine specialist. He could buy a clinic. He does not.

**Psychological impact.** Warren's body is the *most expensively underprotected* on the team. He carries the team financially, administratively, and infrastructurally — every hour he spends arranging the operation is an hour he is not spending on recovery — and his post-Champions embarrassment about the period reads, in part, as the recognition of a young man who **let his own body be spent on a unit that did not reciprocate the care**. The orthopedic catastrophe later in his life happens to a man whose first super-team taught him that wings are expendable.

---

## 6. BOBBY DRAKE — MUTANT THERMOREGULATION, DEVELOPMENTAL ARREST

**Baseline.** Mutant, late adolescence; cryokinetic with ambient-thermal manipulation. In the Champions period, well short of his eventual Omega-tier expression — he ices over for combat but does not yet sustain the full-organic-ice transformation that becomes standard in his later eras. Baseline-human-plus in conditioning, normal skeletal and metabolic profile underneath the ice.

**Thermoregulatory cost.** Sustained cryokinetic output draws on body heat and caloric reserves in ways the team does not schedule for. He runs cold for hours after heavy use. He eats more than he admits and sleeps poorly after major engagements. None of this is monitored.

**Injury record across the run.** Frostbite-margin damage to fingers and toes from over-extended use (self-resolving but cumulative); concussive injuries; soft-tissue from being thrown — Bobby is, after Romanoff, the most-thrown member of the team. He is also the youngest body on the roster and the one whose musculoskeletal development is still in progress; he is taking adult-tier impacts on a not-yet-adult frame.

**Psychological/developmental.** Bobby is the team's youngest, and the team functions as his second adolescence in a unit that is not equipped to parent. The X-Men at least had Xavier. The Champions have Warren, who is barely older, and Hercules, who is a drinking uncle. Bobby's well-documented later struggles with arrested affective development — the joking-as-defense pattern that follows him for decades — is **incubated in the Champions period**, where the absence of any adult holding environment teaches him that the way to survive a team is to be the one who refuses to be serious. This is a medical fact in the broad sense: a developmental trajectory bent by the social-medical environment of his first non-X-Men workplace.

---

## 7. SHARED EXPOSURES AND ENVIRONMENTAL MEDICINE

**The headquarters.** The team operates out of a Los Angeles facility funded and selected by Warren. There is no on-panel infirmary of clinical grade. There is no decontamination capability for the magical, radiological, or psionic exposures the team routinely sustains. The Pluto engagement alone would, in a competent unit, have triggered a metaphysical-contamination protocol; none exists.

**Repeat exposures during the run.**
- *Olympian / Plutonian energies* (formation arc): unknown long-term effect on non-Olympian physiology. Romanoff, Blaze, Warren, and Bobby all sustained direct exposure. No follow-up.
- *Sentinel anti-mutant ordnance* (terminal arc): Warren and Bobby took direct hits. No bloodwork.
- *Magnetic-field manipulation* and adjacent electromagnetic stressors: Romanoff's equipment (Widow's Line, gauntlet electronics) repeatedly degraded; the medical implications for the human nervous system embedded in those fields are not considered.
- *Demonic ambient radiation*, for lack of a better term, from sustained proximity to a Ghost Rider in transformation: unknown effect on the four non-hosts standing within meters of him for two years. No literature exists. No one looks.

**Nutrition and sleep at unit level.** Meals are ad hoc. There is no shared schedule. Hercules eats and drinks Olympian portions; Warren eats avian-metabolic portions; Bobby eats teenager-plus-cryokinetic portions; Romanoff eats operator-discipline portions; Blaze eats when he remembers. The team never sits down to a meal as a unit on panel in a way that reads as ritual rather than incident. Sleep is solo, irregular, and uncoordinated; there is no watch rotation despite the roster containing the single most qualified person on Earth to design one.

---

## 8. THE MEDICAL META-DIAGNOSIS

Five bodies on five incommensurable scales of damage, metabolism, and recovery; one chronic intoxication normalized as character; one untreated complex-trauma presentation concealed by training; one chronic dissociative possession running without containment protocol; one orthopedically fragile flier used as aerial muscle without sports-medicine support; one still-developing adolescent absorbing adult impacts in lieu of an adult holding environment. **No physician of record. No infirmary of clinical grade. No exposure follow-up. No nutrition plan. No sleep doctrine. No protocol for the predictable medical events the roster guarantees.**

The medical history of the Champions is, in the end, the history of a unit that **mistook the absence of immediate fatality for health**. Hercules's invulnerability set the team's pain calibration; everyone else paid the difference in untracked debt. The retrospective embarrassment that every survivor carries about the Champions period is, read somatically, the embarrassment of having lent one's body to a unit that could not be trusted with it — and of having known, on some pre-verbal level, that one was doing so the whole time.

— UATU, observing.


## Somatic Atlas

# SOMATIC ATLAS — THE CHAMPIONS (Los Angeles, Original Roster)

*A total-surveillance file does not record what a body means; it records what a body does, at what frequency, in what posture, with what tell preceding what action. This atlas inventories the Champions as five bodies sharing a room — the gestures each one repeats unconsciously, the way those gestures change when the room temperature shifts from idle to threat to intimacy, and the group-level somatic choreography that emerges when they are all present at once. Where canon shows it on panel, it is cited as observed; where canon implies it consistently across the run, it is logged as pattern.*

---

## 1. THE GROUP BODY — STANDING FORMATION AND PROXEMICS

**Default room geometry.** Place the five Champions in a single space (briefing room, Warren's funded headquarters off Sunset, the *Champions* #11 press conference set) and a stable polygon emerges within forty seconds. Hercules occupies the visual center — he does not choose this; the others *cede* it, drifting outward as he plants. Warren takes the high ground (perched on a desk edge, a chair-back, a window-sill — any surface that elevates him six to ten inches above floor-standing peers; a wing-bearer's reflex toward perch). Bobby orbits Warren at roughly arm's length, almost always to Warren's left, a position canon repeats with such consistency it functions as a uniform. Natasha selects the seat or stance with the clearest sightline to **every exit and every other team member** — never the centermost seat, never against an interior wall, always angled. Johnny stands apart by three to five feet more than social convention would dictate; the others unconsciously do not close that distance.

**The polygon is not symmetric.** Hercules-Warren-Bobby form one tight triangle (the affiliative cluster); Natasha and Johnny are the two isolates, each calibrating distance for different reasons (her: tradecraft; him: containment). Surveillance footage of any unscripted Champions gathering will show this shape forming, dissolving when one member leaves the room, and reforming the instant the fifth re-enters.

**Touch budget.** Per hour of co-presence in non-crisis state: Warren initiates light contact (shoulder pat, arm-touch) approximately six to ten times, distributed almost exclusively to Bobby and Hercules. Hercules initiates contact at higher force and lower frequency — the bear-clasp, the shoulder-grip that staggers the recipient — perhaps two to four times per hour, distributed to all members but Natasha. Bobby reciprocates Warren but rarely initiates. **Natasha initiates zero unsolicited contact** with team members across the entire run; when she touches a teammate it is purposive (medical, tactical, redirective). Johnny initiates contact essentially never; the Zarathos containment problem has trained his body out of casual touch.

**Eye-line economy.** In conversation the team's gaze defaults to Hercules when he is speaking, to Warren when funding or logistics are discussed, to Natasha when threat is mentioned, and **away** from Johnny when his name comes up unbidden — a micro-aversion none of them are aware of and all of them perform.

---

## 2. HERCULES — THE OLYMPIAN BODY

**Baseline posture.** Weight on the back foot, chest deployed forward, chin slightly elevated (eight to twelve degrees above neutral) — the heroic-statue stance, held involuntarily even when seated. He cannot slouch; the musculature does not permit a posture that reads as defeated. Arms cross at the chest or rest with hands on hips with kingly frequency; the akimbo is his default conversational stance.

**Gait.** A heel-strike heavier than his weight should explain — Olympian density loads each step. Floorboards in the team's headquarters audibly register his approach; teammates know who is coming down a corridor without looking. Stride length exceeds Warren's by roughly twenty percent and Bobby's by twenty-five; in group movement Hercules is always either slightly ahead or visibly pacing himself with conscious throttle.

**Hands.** Constantly occupied — a wine-cup, a haunch of food, a club, a thrown object, a clapped shoulder. When unoccupied the hands knead air, flex, or seek the beard. **The beard-stroke** is his thinking-tell: a slow downward draw of thumb and forefinger from cheekbone to chin-point, repeated three to five times before he speaks at length.

**Facial pattern.** Default expression is broad amusement — mouth slightly open, eyes narrowed in pleasure. Genuine anger shows first in the **brow gathering at the bridge of the nose** and the upper lip lifting from the canine; a second-stage anger drops the chin and squares the shoulders. Surprise is theatrical — full eye-widening, head-back recoil, hand to chest. He has not learned to micro-express because he has never needed to deceive anyone.

**Speech somatics.** Voice pitched to project; he speaks at a volume calibrated for an amphitheater regardless of room size. Sentences finish on a falling tone with a slight chest-puff. Laughter is the famous booming **"Ho! Ho!"** — diaphragmatic, head thrown back, accompanied by a thigh- or table-slap that bruises wood.

**Grooming.** Beard combed but not styled; hair shoulder-length, often unwashed for days, then washed conspicuously and re-oiled. Wears the classical tunic-and-sandals by preference and modern dress only under explicit social pressure — Warren has twice provided suits that Hercules wore once.

**Sleep.** Sleeps prodigiously when he sleeps — eleven to fourteen hours, prone, mouth open, sonorous. Goes three to four days without sleep when engaged in revelry or combat with no apparent decrement. Wakes instantly to threat with no transitional grogginess.

**Eating.** Caloric intake estimated in the tens of thousands per day; eats with hands by preference, utensils when reminded. Tears bread, gnaws bone, drinks from the bottle. Eats fast, then sits with hands folded over a distended belly. No food aversions observed.

**Sexual.** Catholic in appetite, indiscriminate in selection, unsubtle in approach — pursues with verbal declaration rather than seduction; rejection produces brief theatrical lament and immediate redirection. No observed possessiveness, no observed jealousy regarding team members' partnerships.

**Substance.** Wine continuously, from morning. Hand reaches for a cup roughly every twelve to fifteen minutes when present at the headquarters. Functional through quantities that would kill a baseline human; the **only behavioral shift** under intoxication is increased volume and reduced verbal economy.

**Shifts by state:**
- *Stress:* the akimbo tightens to fists-on-hips; beard-stroke accelerates; volume climbs.
- *Threat:* immediate forward weight-shift, hand to weapon or to the air where a weapon should be; broad grin appears (combat is *pleasure*).
- *Intimacy:* unexpected gentleness — the hand that crushes pavement will rest on a forearm with the weight of a glove. Voice drops a full octave.
- *Wounded pride (Natasha elected leader, #4):* shoulders square but turn three-quarters away from the offending party; chin drops rather than lifts; the only posture in which he resembles a sulking child.

---

## 3. BLACK WIDOW — THE TRAINED BODY

**Baseline posture.** Spine neutral, shoulders dropped, weight distributed evenly across both feet — the posture of someone who could move in any direction in any instant and does not wish to telegraph which. She *does not lean.* Against walls, against counters, against doorframes — never. Leaning surrenders a hundredth of a second of reaction time, and the Red Room trained that hundredth out of her by age fourteen.

**Gait.** Quiet to the point that teammates startle when she enters a room. Heel-toe roll with the weight rolling along the outer edge of the foot first — a fighter's walk and a tracker's walk. Stride length consistent regardless of urgency; she does not run unless she must, and when she runs it is full sprint, no intermediate gear.

**Hands.** At rest, hands hang or settle lightly on her thighs, palms inward, fingers slightly curled — within a quarter-second of a grip. She does not gesture while speaking; the hands stay still and the face does the work. **Tell:** when calculating, her right index finger taps her own left wrist (where the Widow's Bite sits) — three taps, pause, three taps, a metronome she does not know she runs.

**Facial pattern.** Default expression is *neutral pleasant* — slight upward turn at the mouth corners, eyes soft-focused, brow unmoved. This is a manufactured baseline; her *actual* resting face (observed in solitude, mirror scenes in her solo features) is harder, mouth flatter, eyes harder-focused. She wears the pleasant mask continuously in team settings. Genuine emotion shows in the **eyes only** — pupil dilation under attraction or fear, brow micro-tension at threat, a very brief downward gaze when grief surfaces. The mouth almost never moves involuntarily.

**Speech somatics.** Voice low, controlled, contralto, with the residual Russian shaping consonants she has chosen not to fully eliminate. She speaks at a volume requiring her listener to lean toward her — a deliberate dominance behavior she absorbed from her handlers and has never discarded. Pauses are weaponized; she will hold silence past social comfort.

**Grooming.** Daily, meticulous, never observed in a non-presentable state on panel. Hair (red, shoulder-length to mid-back depending on era) brushed and arranged with attention; nails kept short and unpainted — operational. Wears the catsuit on duty; off-duty wardrobe is high-end, monochromatic, fitted, and **always permits full range of motion.** No restrictive jewelry, no heels she cannot fight in.

**Sleep.** Light sleeper, four to six hours by preference, often segmented (two-three hours, wake, perimeter, two-three more). Sleeps on her side facing the room's primary entry. Wakes fully alert with weapon in hand within a second of any anomalous sound — a behavior that briefly terrified Bobby during a shared-quarters incident the team handled by never assigning them adjacent rooms again.

**Eating.** Disciplined. Portions calibrated, protein-forward, alcohol limited to a single glass in public settings (a tradecraft choice — never matches a counterpart drink-for-drink). Eats fast and efficiently in private; eats slowly and observantly in company, using the meal as an information-gathering frame.

**Sexual.** Reads as continuously available and is in fact carefully selective; the availability is the cover, the selectivity is the truth. Initiates touch with intent and withdraws cleanly. Post-Murdock and pre-Champions, she is in a low-affect refractory period; on-panel she does not pursue romantic interest within the team and rebuffs Hercules's overtures with practiced grace and zero offense taken.

**Substance.** Nicotine in earlier eras (declining through the 70s), minimal alcohol, no recreational drugs — the Red Room's pharmacological history left her with a permanent wariness of altered states.

**Shifts by state:**
- *Stress:* the wrist-tap accelerates; jaw sets at the masseter; breathing slows and deepens rather than quickens.
- *Threat:* immediate weight-shift to a fighting base, hands rise to mid-line, face goes *flatter* — the pleasant mask drops and reveals nothing under it. This is the most frightening thing about her in the room.
- *Intimacy:* the mask does not so much drop as *soften* — eyes hold longer, voice drops half a register, a hand will rest on the other party's forearm and remain there. Selective, rare, intentional.
- *Command challenge (Hercules contests her field-leader role, recurring):* she does not escalate. Posture remains neutral, voice drops further, eye contact extends. She wins these by refusing to perform winning.

---

## 4. GHOST RIDER (JOHNNY BLAZE) — THE HAUNTED BODY

**Baseline posture.** Closed. Shoulders forward and rolled inward, arms often crossed over the sternum or tucked under armpits, hands frequently in pockets or jacket folds — a containment posture. He sits with knees together more often than apart. The body of a man trying to take up less space than he occupies, because something else inside him takes up more.

**Gait.** Stuntman's gait — balanced, slightly bow-legged from years on a bike, weight low. Carries himself with an athlete's economy. When the sun sets his stride shortens by roughly fifteen percent; teammates have noted (and never named) that Johnny walks differently in the dark.

**Hands.** Restless. Fingers tap thighs, drum surfaces, work at the seam of his jeans. **Two specific tells:** (1) a recurrent rubbing of the right palm with the left thumb — friction over the spot where, in his felt-sense, the bargain was sealed; (2) intermittent flexion of the jaw muscle visible at the temple, the **trigeminal clench** that precedes a transformation by approximately ninety seconds.

**Facial pattern.** Default expression is *tired* — eyes slightly hooded, mouth in a thin line, jaw set. Smiles when he remembers to and the smile does not reach the eyes. Laughs short and sharp, single exhalations rather than sustained mirth. The **pre-transformation facial sequence** is documented across the run: pupils blow wide, sclera darken, jaw drops by perhaps a centimeter, head tilts back five to ten degrees; the skull is visible under the skin for one panel before it *is* the skin.

**Speech somatics.** Low-register, slow cadence, working-class American Southwest vowels. Speaks less than any other team member, by margin — perhaps a quarter of Hercules's word-count per shared scene. Sentences are short. Pauses are not strategic (as with Natasha) but distractive — he is listening to something the others cannot hear.

**Grooming.** Adequate but distracted. Hair clean but rarely styled; stubble at one-to-three days perpetually. Wears the leather jacket and jeans as a uniform regardless of occasion. The leather smells of gasoline and something else teammates do not name.

**Sleep.** Erratic and poor. Three to five hours, broken, often dreamt-through. Sleeps clothed or partially clothed in case of nocturnal transformation. Avoids shared sleeping arrangements categorically. The bedroom Warren assigned him is sparsely furnished and has burn-marks on the wall above the headboard that no one has asked about.

**Eating.** Underweight for his frame. Eats when reminded, prefers diner food, drinks coffee continuously. Appetite suppressed by chronic dread.

**Sexual.** Faithful in intent to Roxanne Simpson; geographically and metaphysically separated from her throughout the Champions period. On-panel he does not pursue and is not pursued — the containment posture extends to the erotic. His body is not available to be wanted because it is not always his.

**Substance.** Coffee at high volume. Beer occasionally and never more than two. Cigarette in earlier eras, tapering. Avoids anything that compromises vigilance — vigilance is the only thing keeping the second occupant down.

**Shifts by state:**
- *Stress:* palm-rubbing accelerates; jaw-clench visible; he goes quieter rather than louder.
- *Threat:* a pause — the visible internal negotiation — and then either flight to a safer distance (to transform without civilian risk) or the full transformation cycle (head-back, flame-eruption from the cranium, leather sealing into the Spirit's aesthetic, voice dropping into the Zarathos register, which is not Johnny's voice and which the team has learned to never quite address).
- *Intimacy:* almost none observed within team. With Roxanne in flashback and bracketing scenes: the closed posture opens — shoulders drop back, hands accept being held, the tired face softens. The transformation suppressor in her presence is observable as a postural unlock.
- *Post-transformation:* exhausted, often nauseated, occasionally weeping silently and briefly. Wants to be alone. The team learned in the first two issues to allow this.

---

## 5. ICEMAN (BOBBY DRAKE) — THE ADOLESCENT BODY

**Baseline posture.** Loose, slumped, perpetually on the verge of horizontal. Bobby slouches in chairs to a degree that approaches the recumbent; sits on tables, leans against doorframes, drapes over furniture. The body language of a young man who has not yet decided his body is a serious instrument.

**Gait.** Bouncy, light, slightly forward-leaning. Hands often in pockets. Skids the last step of a stairway descent for the small physical pleasure of the skid.

**Hands.** **Constantly producing ice** as fidget — small spheres rolled between fingers, miniature sculptures formed and dissolved, ice-cube absentmindedly crushed in palm. This is the most diagnostic single behavior on the team: when Bobby is anxious, the room's ambient temperature drops by one to two degrees. When he is content, frost forms in tiny ferns along the surface his hand rests on. Teammates *read the windows* to know his state.

**Facial pattern.** Mobile, expressive, telegraphic — the opposite of Natasha. Eyebrows up at surprise, mouth open in delight, full grimace at displeasure, easy laugh that crinkles the eyes. Wears his thoughts on his face. **Ice-form facial pattern** is necessarily flatter — facial musculature reads through the ice as gross shapes only, which means in combat his most expressive feature is **silenced**, and the others miss it without noticing they miss it.

**Speech somatics.** Quick, joking, deflective. Joke-rate elevated in proportion to discomfort — when Bobby is *cracking wise* at five-second intervals, something is wrong. New York-inflected, mid-Atlantic by Champions-era exposure, vowels slightly Southern Californianizing across the run. Voice has not fully settled into adult register; cracks occasionally under stress.

**Grooming.** Casual. Showers daily, hair tousled rather than styled, clothes off-the-rack and Warren-influenced (Warren occasionally buys Bobby clothes; Bobby wears them; Bobby buys nothing similar himself). No facial hair attempted across the run.

**Sleep.** Eight to ten hours by preference, sleeps deeply, hard to wake. Sleeps cool — the room he sleeps in registers below ambient, and bedding develops light frost by morning. Wakes slowly with a stretch and a yawn that the team has heard often enough to mimic affectionately behind his back.

**Eating.** Cold foods preferred — ice cream, cereal, sodas. Eats constantly between meals. Burns calories at a metabolic rate elevated by his power-use. Underfed during arcs of heavy ice-form deployment.

**Sexual.** Late-blooming, anxious, performing more confidence than he has. Looks at women in the room and looks away when caught. Pursues with humor as cover; the humor is the pursuit *and* the retreat. Does not pursue within team.

**Substance.** Beer at parties; nothing harder. Caffeine moderate. The youngest body on the team and the one with the least pharmacological history.

**Shifts by state:**
- *Stress:* joke-rate climbs, ambient temperature drops, ice-fidgets accelerate; the *ferns on the window* are the earliest warning sign of group tension Bobby has registered before anyone else has spoken it.
- *Threat:* ice-form snaps on in a wave from the chest outward, hands first, in approximately one second; the slouch vanishes immediately, posture squares.
- *Intimacy:* warmer in every sense — temperature normalizes around him, fidgets stop, eye contact lengthens. He is a young man whose body is happiest when someone else's body is nearby and unguarded.
- *Hurt feelings (Warren's attention diverted, Hercules's casual dismissals):* the slouch deepens, the jokes get sharper-edged, frost appears unprompted on a glass he is not holding.

---

## 6. ANGEL (WARREN WORTHINGTON III) — THE WINGED BODY

**Baseline posture.** Open, upright, *display.* Warren stands as if his portrait is being painted at all times — shoulders back, chest forward, chin level, a posture refined by twenty years of debutante training and reinforced by the literal need to balance two large mobile appendages on his back. He does not slouch even in private; the wings make slouching uncomfortable.

**Gait.** Athletic, slightly long-strided, with a barely-perceptible **shoulder roll** at each step — the involuntary micro-articulation of the wing-base muscles balancing weight. Observers who do not know what they are looking at register him as *graceful*; observers who know read the constant wing-management.

**Hands.** Expressive, mid-range gestures while speaking, palms-up frequently — the open-handed gesture of someone who has never had to convince anyone he isn't holding a weapon. Touches teammates easily on shoulders, forearms, occasionally hair (Bobby specifically). The Worthington money is in the hands too — manicured nails, a watch worth more than the headquarters.

**Wings.** A continuous somatic vocabulary the team has learned to read without realizing it: 
- *Folded tight to back:* baseline calm.
- *Slight outward flare (six to eight inches):* engaged interest.
- *Half-mantled (half-extended, raised slightly):* irritation or territorial display.
- *Full mantle:* alarm, threat-response, or anger.
- *Drooping below the shoulder line:* exhaustion, depression, or shame.
- *One wing flicked sharply:* the equivalent of a teammate snapping fingers — used to redirect attention, almost always toward Bobby.

The wings also **groom themselves involuntarily** — Warren preens at the primary feathers with one hand while distracted, a behavior he is faintly embarrassed about and does in private more than in company.

**Facial pattern.** Patrician — high cheekbones, clear eyes, easy smile that *does* reach the eyes (unlike Johnny's). Genuine warmth in default expression. Frowns rarely; when he frowns, the brow furrows symmetrically and the team registers it as a serious data point.

**Speech somatics.** Mid-Atlantic prep-school diction softened by California exposure. Speaks with the cadence of someone whose words have always been listened to — no rush, no defensive overlap, no need to interrupt. Asks questions and waits for answers. The most well-mannered speaker on the team by a wide margin.

**Grooming.** Immaculate. Showers twice daily (the wings require it — feathers retain ambient odors). Hair (blond, conservative cut) trimmed to schedule. Wardrobe expensive and considered; civilian dress is *bespoke* and accommodates the wings via specially-tailored slits with discreet closures.

**Sleep.** Seven to eight hours, prone or on the side, never on the back (impossible with the wings). Sleeps deeply, in expensive bedding,


## Attachment & Relational Patterns

# ATTACHMENT & RELATIONAL PATTERNS — THE CHAMPIONS (LA, Original Roster)

*Filed as Section 6 of the standing dossier. Cross-references §3 (Psychological) and §4 (Psychiatric) but treats attachment in its own right: how this five-body organism reaches for, holds, distrusts, wounds, and tries to mend its bonds — internally among members, externally to the world, and across the longitudinal record from 1975 to the present scattered cameos.*

---

## 1. ATTACHMENT STYLE — CLASSIFICATION AND ORIGIN

### 1.1 The classification, stated plainly

The Champions, considered as a single attaching organism, present a **disorganized attachment style with a fearful-avoidant surface and an anxious-preoccupied interior**. In Main/Hesse terms: the group simultaneously seeks and fears proximity to its own members. In Bartholomew's four-quadrant frame: the team's *model of self* is negative (we do not actually know who we are; we suspect we are not enough), and its *model of other* is split — combat-positive, civilian-negative. They trust each other to catch a falling body and not to remember a birthday.

This is not idiosyncratic to one member. It is the **group's** style, generated by the additive resonance of five individual attachment histories that happen to harmonize on exactly the wrong frequency.

### 1.2 The five intake histories — what each member brought to the door

The team's attachment pathology is over-determined because **every founding member arrived pre-wounded in the same week of their life**. Read individually these are coincidences; read as an intake cohort they are a clinical pattern.

- **Warren Worthington III** — recently de-mothered by the X-Men's hiatus, raised in a household where money substituted for presence, attaches through *provision* (he buys the headquarters, he funds the jet, he pays the staff). His attachment template is **caregiving-as-belonging**: I am loved if I am useful, and useful means paying. This is anxious-preoccupied in the classic sense, performed in the idiom of philanthropy.
- **Bobby Drake** — junior partner in the Worthington dyad, attaches *through* Warren rather than to the team directly. His template is **little-brother appendage**: bond to the bond, not to the unit. The humor is a regulation device, not an offering. He is the team's youngest attachment-age, functionally pre-adolescent in his bid for belonging.
- **Natasha Romanoff** — the most recently and visibly ruptured (Murdock having left her with the apartment keys and a published goodbye), arrives with a *lifetime* training in instrumental relationship: the Red Room curriculum is, among other things, a course in counterfeit attachment. Her template is **withhold, observe, withdraw**: bond only to those whose ulterior motives you can map. The Champions, having none, are uniquely illegible to her.
- **Johnny Blaze** — engaged to Roxanne, possessed by Zarathos, embedded in a Hollywood stunt circuit that does not know what he is. His template is **bond at one remove**: never let the person close enough to be inside the blast radius. He arrives at the team already curating who can be allowed near him on a full-moon equivalent.
- **Hercules** — periodically exiled from Olympus, his attachment template is **god-among-mortals tourism**: bonds are real but bounded by the certainty that he will outlive them and return upstairs. He attaches *broadly and shallowly* by Olympian habit. The "broadly" reads to mortals as warmth; the "shallowly" reads, on reflection, as the loneliest member of the team.

The compositional fact: **no member arrived with a secure base in working order**. There was no one in the room with a functional template to model. A group can borrow secure attachment from a single member who has it (this is, arguably, what Reed Richards is for the Fantastic Four, what Xavier *attempts* for the X-Men). The Champions had no such donor.

### 1.3 The birth-trauma imprint

The team formed mid-attack. The first shared experience was not introduction, negotiation, or meal — it was *combat triage of strangers*. This becomes the **somatic template of bonding for the entire run**: the group only *feels like itself* when something is exploding. Between explosions, members revert to their pre-team isolation patterns. The birth-trauma imprint is observable in panel after panel: down-time scenes are stiff, the dialogue is stagey, members exit rooms early. Combat scenes are loose, fluent, intimate.

This is the relational analog of a couple who only feel married during the fight.

---

## 2. HOW THEY BOND

### 2.1 The three observable bonding modalities

1. **Combat-fusion bonding.** Under fire the team achieves a near-instantaneous tactical intimacy that outstrips its actual relational depth. By issue #6 they are catching each other's cues at a level usually requiring a year's training. This is real, and it is the team's one undeniable competence. It is also the *only* register in which they have ever practiced being together.
2. **Provision bonding (Warren-mediated).** Warren expresses affection through infrastructure — the LA HQ, the salaries (yes, the team is partially salaried, a fact Warren minimizes), the catering, the press apparatus. The others accept the provision and reciprocate by *not noticing* the asymmetry. Acceptance-without-acknowledgment is the local dialect of love.
3. **Adjacent-presence bonding.** Members occupy the same room without engagement and count it as together-time. Bobby in front of a TV, Natasha reading at the window, Warren at a desk, Hercules at the bar, Blaze on the balcony — the most relationally healthy scenes in the run are actually these: low-demand co-presence. The team has, almost by accident, discovered the introvert's bonding mode. They never name it as such.

### 2.2 Bonding is *triadic*, never dyadic

A telling structural feature: the Champions have **no stable dyads**. Warren-Bobby is the closest, imported from the X-Men, and even it gets diluted in LA. Otherwise, members interact almost exclusively in *threes or more*. Natasha and Hercules are rarely alone on panel without a third. Blaze and anyone is almost always mediated by the scene's tactical context.

This triadic preference is diagnostic. Dyads require negotiated intimacy; triads diffuse it. The Champions, unable to sustain dyadic depth, organize relationally as *constellations* — easier to be a star in a sky than a partner in a room.

### 2.3 What bonding looks like at the molecular level

- **Hercules** initiates with grand gestures (toast, embrace, boast); receives bonding poorly when offered quietly. Reads silence as rejection. Drinks more when ignored.
- **Natasha** initiates almost never; receives by *staying in the room* — her bonding signal is non-departure. The others learn, slowly, to read her presence as affection. None learn this fully.
- **Warren** initiates by *organizing* — proposing the outing, picking up the tab, scheduling the photo op. Receives bonding through being thanked. Thanked rarely. Compensates by organizing more.
- **Bobby** initiates by joking and physical proximity (he is the team's most spatially close member, the one most likely to drape on furniture near someone else); receives by being laughed *with*. Laughed *at* shuts him down for hours.
- **Blaze** initiates by withdrawing in a way that invites pursuit, then withdrawing further when pursued. Receives by being left a single specific accommodation (a chair facing the door, a meal saved). Nobody on the team learns this either.

The team is, in attachment terms, **five people speaking five different love-languages, none of whom ever sat down to learn the others'**. They bond anyway, in the gaps.

---

## 3. HOW THEY DISTRUST

### 3.1 The architecture of distrust

Distrust in the Champions is **lateral, low-volume, and chronic** rather than acute. No member ever sits across from another and says "I don't trust you." Instead, distrust is expressed through:

- **Tactical preemption.** Natasha consistently positions herself to handle the move *before* Hercules makes it, an unmistakable signal that she does not trust his judgment in nuanced engagements. Hercules does not perceive the signal because he reads her positioning as initiative on his behalf.
- **Information asymmetry.** Natasha does not brief the team on her contacts, intelligence sources, or background. She justifies this as tradecraft; functionally, it is a refusal of attachment. The team does not press, which is its own refusal in return.
- **Containment vigilance.** Warren and Bobby track Blaze's mood as a proxy for Zarathos's proximity. Neither says so. Blaze knows. Nobody discusses it.
- **Financial euphemism.** Hercules, Natasha, and Blaze never ask Warren what the operation costs. The not-asking is a distrust signal — they suspect the answer would obligate them, and they decline the obligation by declining the question.

### 3.2 The two persons specifically not trusted

1. **Hercules** is not trusted with *nuance*. Cosmically, with strength, yes. With diplomacy, intelligence, women in distress, alcohol-adjacent decision-making — no. The team works around him constantly. He notices intermittently and is wounded.
2. **Blaze** is not trusted with *himself*. The team treats him as a load-bearing wall that might give way. They do not exclude him, but they do not include him in planning at the level his combat contribution warrants. He notices fully and isolates further.

### 3.3 Distrust is never repaired because never named

The Champions have **no repair vocabulary**. Across seventeen issues there are essentially zero scenes of explicit interpersonal repair — no apologies, no naming of injuries, no "we need to talk." Repair, where it happens, is **somatic and indirect**: a shared meal after a hard mission, a wordless shoulder-clap, Hercules pouring an extra glass and pushing it across the bar without comment.

This is a workable repair register *if everyone speaks it*. They do not. Bobby in particular needs verbal repair and does not get it; he learns to suppress the need. Natasha needs no repair at all (her template treats injury as data); she becomes the inadvertent model the others over-imitate, suppressing their own legitimate repair needs because the most opaque member appears not to require any.

---

## 4. HOW THEY BETRAY

### 4.1 Betrayal in the small key

There is no Judas in the Champions. There is, instead, **a constant low-grade betrayal-of-attention** — members failing to show up *fully* for each other in ways that, summed across a year, constitute a quiet abandonment.

Specific patterns:

- **Warren's checkbook substitutes for his presence.** Funding the team is, partially, a way of not being available to it relationally. He is on panel often; he is *with* the others rarely. The check is a kindness and a withdrawal in one motion.
- **Natasha's compartmentalization is a soft betrayal of the team's stated democracy.** A team that elected her field leader (#4) deserves her intelligence picture. She does not provide it. This is not malice; it is her template. The team is betrayed by her professionalism.
- **Hercules's intoxication is a betrayal of operational readiness.** He shows up to fights with wine in his system. The others adjust. The adjustment is itself the betrayal — by accommodating, they cosign his unavailability.
- **Blaze's containment failures betray the mandate.** Each uncontrolled Zarathos episode is, in the strict sense, a violation of the "for the common man" promise. The team absorbs each episode without protocol revision. The promise is betrayed structurally and continuously.
- **Bobby's joking deflection betrays the seriousness of his own contributions.** He is the youngest, the most powerful in latent potential, and the one most likely to undercut himself before others can. The team accepts this self-diminishment, which is a betrayal of him by inaction.

### 4.2 The structural betrayal

The deepest betrayal is **collective and against the team itself**: every member's failure to insist that the Champions become more than a rebound. Each individually knows, at some level, that the formation is provisional. Each privately keeps an exit. Romanoff returns to solo work the moment a credible re-attachment opens. Warren goes back to the X-Men adjacency the moment it reconstitutes. Bobby follows Warren. Blaze returns to the road. Hercules returns to Olympus.

None of these are dramatic departures. None are framed as betrayals. **That is the betrayal**: the team's eventual scattering is treated by every member as natural, even welcome, which means each was, all along, planning the exit while inside the bond. This is the relational signature of a rebound — and the canonical retrospective embarrassment (Warren especially, but also Bobby and Natasha when pressed) is the late recognition of having been, themselves, the betrayers.

### 4.3 External betrayal — the Rampage case

The Champions' most consequential *betrayed party* is not a member but a foe: **Rampage**. A bankrupted small businessman, the literal demographic the team exists for, encounters the Champions as a wall of force rather than a hand. The team's failure to recognize him as their constituency rather than their adversary is a *moral* betrayal of the mandate. His radicalization on second appearance is the team's stated mission returning as enemy combatant. The team never integrates the feedback. This is the team's relational template applied outward: *we do not, in fact, know how to bond with the people we said we were here for.*

---

## 5. HOW THEY REPAIR

### 5.1 Repair modalities, ranked by frequency

1. **Shared mission** (extremely high frequency). When friction rises, the team takes a case. The case discharges the affect via fight-flight. The friction *appears* repaired because the symptoms remit. The wound is not closed; it is shelved.
2. **Hercules-led carouse** (moderate frequency). After a difficult engagement, Hercules organizes food and drink. This works for him, Bobby, and intermittently Warren. It does not work for Natasha or Blaze, who attend and remain unrepaired.
3. **Warren's logistical apology** (moderate frequency). When Warren senses he has imposed, he upgrades the infrastructure — better quarters, better gear, better PR. The others read this correctly as apology and accept it. Nothing is said.
4. **Adjacent silence** (low frequency, high efficacy). The team's actual best repair moments are wordless co-presence in the aftermath of a near-loss. These are also the team's most relationally adult moments in the run.
5. **Verbal repair** (essentially absent). Across seventeen issues, the count of explicit "I'm sorry / I was wrong / I'm hurt" beats among members is vanishingly low.

### 5.2 Repair failures

The team **cannot repair the Hercules/Romanoff command rupture** because repair would require Hercules to acknowledge a subordinate leadership and Natasha to claim it openly. Neither happens. The rupture is managed rather than mended, by routing around it issue by issue.

The team **cannot repair the Blaze containment problem** because repair would require naming the problem. Naming would shame Blaze. Shaming Blaze would risk the very episode the containment is meant to prevent. The team is locked in a no-repair loop driven by the kindness of silence.

The team **cannot repair its mandate failure** because the mandate is Warren's, and to revise it would be to demote him from primary author of the team's identity to one voice among five. The team protects Warren's authorship by leaving the mandate unrepaired.

### 5.3 The one durable repair

The genuine, lasting interpersonal repair the team accomplishes is **between Warren and Bobby**, who arrive in LA in mid-quarrel (the post-X-Men drift had strained them) and leave the Champions era closer than they began. The team functioned, in this single dyad, as a successful holding environment. It is meaningful that the team's *only* durable relational achievement is the one bond it inherited rather than created.

---

## 6. INTIMACY AND DEPENDENCY PATTERNS

### 6.1 Intimacy is somatic and tactical, never biographical

The Champions know each other's **fighting styles intimately and their childhoods not at all**. The team has detailed, lived knowledge of each member's reach, range, reaction time, ice-pattern preference, wing-beat tempo, hammer-grip, garrote-hand, hellfire-radius. The team has essentially no working knowledge of each member's family, history, fears, romantic past, or interior life.

This is **inverted intimacy** — depth in the operational register, shallowness in the personal. It is the intimacy profile of veterans rather than of friends. It is workable in war and lonely in peace.

### 6.2 Dependency — covert, asymmetric, and load-bearing on Warren

Officially the team is a collective. Operationally it depends on:

- **Warren** for infrastructure and money. Without him: dissolution within weeks.
- **Hercules** for raw force and figurehead presence. Without him: tactical viability collapses against any heavy threat.
- **Natasha** for actual command competence. Without her: missions degrade into brawls.
- **Bobby** for crowd control, mobility logistics, comic relief regulation. Without him: tone darkens past public palatability.
- **Blaze** for terror-effect and supernatural-tier engagement. Without him: a class of threats becomes unmanageable.

Every member is load-bearing. **No member admits to depending on any other.** The dependency is structurally complete and verbally denied. This is a textbook **counter-dependent** group culture — high actual need, high denial of need.

### 6.3 The romantic dimension

Notably **the team contains no internal romantic pairing**. Hercules flirts (Hercules always flirts); Natasha is fresh from Murdock and not available; Warren has Candy Southern off-panel; Bobby is in adolescent romantic chaos with external figures; Blaze is engaged to Roxanne. The absence of internal pairing is, by Marvel-team standards, *unusual* and worth noting: it suggests the team's members did not perceive each other as candidates for *real* intimacy, only for tactical companionship. They were, collectively, treating the team as a transitional object — not a place where new primary attachments would form.

This may be the single most diagnostic fact in the file. **A super-team that produces no romance is a team whose members did not believe in its permanence.**

### 6.4 Dependency on the public

Externally, the team is **dependent on public legitimation** in a way the Avengers are not. The Avengers have the charter. The X-Men have the school. The FF have the building and the name. The Champions have *only the press*. Their dependency on continued favorable coverage is acute and unacknowledged. When the press cools (Rampage's second-appearance coverage, in particular), the team's internal cohesion drops measurably the same week.

---

## 7. THE RELATIONAL TEMPLATE REPEATED ACROSS EVERY RELATIONSHIP

### 7.1 The template, stated

> **Bond rapidly under threat. Do not negotiate the bond's terms. Perform the bond publicly. Sustain it through action rather than speech. Notice no asymmetries. Repair only by routing around. Exit without announcement when a better attachment opens. Later, be quietly embarrassed.**

This template is observable in:

- **Team-to-member relations.** Every member's arc with the team follows this pattern exactly.
- **Member-to-member relations within the team.** The Warren-Hercules, Natasha-Hercules, Bobby-Warren, Blaze-everyone dyads each enact a miniature of the template.
- **Team-to-public relations.** The Champions' relationship to LA is itself this template: a rapid public bond, no terms negotiated with the city, performed visibly, sustained by spectacle, asymmetries (the team is rich and the city is not the "common man") unnoticed, repair routed around (Rampage), exited by cancellation, retrospectively embarrassing.
- **Team-to-peer-team relations.** The Champions' tenuous relationships with the Avengers and X-Men reproduce the template: brief alliances under threat, no formal coordination, performed cordiality, no repair after friction, eventual quiet drift.
- **Team-to-mission relations.** Even the Champions' relationship *to their own cases* follows the template — engage rapidly, do not strategize, perform the win publicly, do not after-action-review, exit, forget. The case-load is itself a series of small rebounds.

### 7.2 Why the template is so consistent

Because the template is **the only template all five members can execute without negotiation**. It is the lowest-common-denominator attachment pattern available to a group containing an avoidant spy, a counter-dependent godling, an over-functioning philanthropist, a dissociation-managing damnation-vehicle, and a deflecting adolescent. The template is the *intersection*, not the *union*, of their relational competencies. The Champions are bonded by what each is *unwilling* to do.

### 7.3 The template's tell

The diagnostic feature that confirms the template is operating: **the embarrassment**. Healthy attachments leave nostalgia; rebound attachments leave embarrassment. The unanimity of the survivors' embarrassment about the Champions era — across Warren's later titles, Bobby's, Natasha's silences, Hercules's and Blaze's near-total non-mention — is the long-tail evidence that every member privately knew, at the time, that they were running this template rather than building a real attachment. The embarrassment is the *recognition*, decades downstream, of one's own complicity in a relational shortcut.

### 7.4 The template's grace note

And yet — the template, for all its limits, was not nothing. Five people in the worst week of their separately wounded years walked into a fight together and stayed in it for two years. The bonds were thin but real. The combat-intimacy was earned. The Warren-Bobby repair was completed. The fact that none of them would do it that way again is not a verdict on what happened; it is the standard testimony of survivors who learned, from a relationship that should not have worked, what they would require of the next one.

The Champions are, in attachment terms, **everyone's first apartment after the breakup**: too expensive, too loud, too crowded, too soon, full of people you would not have chosen if you had been thinking clearly, and the place you go quiet about later not because it was bad but because it was the proof that you had not yet learned to live alone.

— UATU, observing.


## Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

# SECTION 6 — DEFENSES & COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS

## Preamble: How a Group Defends Itself

A group's defensive architecture is not the sum of its members' individual defenses; it is the *negotiated stack* of operations the group implicitly authorizes to keep its self-concept stable, its anxieties unspoken, and its dissolution out of view. The Champions, as established, formed in a state of collective recent loss, with no shared ethical framework, no command doctrine, and no institutional infrastructure beyond Warren Worthington's checkbook. A group that fragile generates a *thick* defensive layer almost immediately, and the Champions do — visible on nearly every page of the 17-issue run, and audible in the long silence that follows.

What follows is the full inventory: the negative (pathological) defenses ranked from most primitive to most mature, then the positive (genuinely adaptive) compensatory mechanisms, then the meta-level defenses that operate at the *structure* of the team rather than at any single behavioral seam. Each is tied to specific in-canon behavior.

---

## 6.1 PRIMITIVE DEFENSES (Level 1 — Psychotic / Pre-Oedipal Register)

These are the defenses that distort reality at the perceptual level. The Champions deploy them sparingly but conspicuously when the team's existence itself is threatened.

### 6.1.1 Denial (of formation conditions)

The most foundational and most visible defense. The team *refuses to register* that it was assembled by accident in the middle of someone else's kidnapping. Every retrospective in-universe reference (Warren's, Bobby's, even narrator captions) frames the Champions' founding as an *act* — a *decision* — rather than what it demonstrably was: five strangers ducking the same rubble. The press conferences in #4 and #5, the formal incorporation, the headquarters lease — all of it is the *paperwork of denial*, the bureaucratic post-hoc construction of intentionality where none existed. The team cannot afford to know it was an accident, because to know that would be to ask why it should continue, and no answer to that question exists.

**Behavioral signature:** the team uses the language of *mandate* and *mission* (Warren's verbatim phrasing in #5–7) with a frequency disproportionate to any actual mission-planning behavior. This is denial speaking through repetition.

### 6.1.2 Psychotic-register Splitting (of the Ghost Rider problem)
