Blaze's Zarathos transformation is, clinically, a chronic dissociative crisis with destructive potential in civilian settings — exactly the failure mode the team's stated mandate cannot survive. The team handles it by *splitting the Rider off* from Blaze in their internal representation: when Johnny is Johnny, he is "our friend, the stuntman"; when the Rider manifests, the team narrates it as a discrete weather event, with no continuity to the man. There is no protocol because there is no acknowledged condition. The splitting is so complete that nobody on the roster — not even Romanoff, who has *training* in handling unstable assets — initiates a containment conversation across 17 issues. The threat is psychotically un-seen.

### 6.1.3 Projective Identification (onto the Avengers)

The Champions' allergy to the Avengers, the government, and Establishment heroism more broadly is constant background radiation in the run. The team projects its own deficits — bureaucratic clumsiness, celebrity-as-substance, internal command incoherence — onto the East Coast team and then experiences itself as the *opposite* of what it has just expelled. This is classic projective identification: the unwanted self-content is located in another agent and then *managed* through opposition. Warren in particular speaks of the Avengers with a defensive edge ("we're not like them — we're for the people") that is, on the evidence of the team's actual behavior, not earned.

---

## 6.2 IMMATURE DEFENSES (Level 2 — Borderline Register)

The team's working defensive layer. Most of the team's day-to-day functioning rides on this stack.

### 6.2.1 Acting Out (mission as affect-regulator)

The single most-deployed defense in the Champions' repertoire. Any internal tension — Hercules and Natasha's command friction, Warren and Bobby's identity drift after the X-Men, Blaze's dissociation, public criticism — is *resolved* by taking a mission. The pattern is so reliable it can be diagrammed: tension rises, somebody (usually Hercules) declares the need to "find someone to *fight*," and the team's interior is anesthetized for the duration of the engagement. The Bion fight-flight assumption is the formal name for this; the lived experience inside the team is that *being shot at is easier than being known*.

**Granular instance:** the recurring beat where Hercules and Natasha's leadership dispute is interrupted by an alarm and never resumed. Across the run this happens enough times to constitute a pattern of *strategic interruption* — the team welcomes the alarm.

### 6.2.2 Somatization (the body as the team's emotional vocabulary)

The team cannot speak feeling, but it bleeds plentifully. Hercules's injuries (which he metabolizes effortlessly), Iceman's overexertions, Angel's wing strain, Blaze's transformations, Romanoff's catalog of bruises — these are presented panel after panel and processed by the team primarily through *physical* attention: bandaging, recovery rooms, debriefs framed around tactical injury rather than psychological aftermath. The team has a *medbay vocabulary* and no *clinical* one. Affect lives in the body because there is nowhere else for it to live.

### 6.2.3 Passive Aggression (Bobby's joke register; Natasha's withdrawal)

Iceman's persistent comedic deflation of serious moments and Black Widow's silent disengagements are the team's two primary passive-aggressive registers. Bobby's jokes consistently arrive when emotional intimacy is about to be established and *break* the moment — this is not a personality tic, it is a *role* the group has implicitly assigned him: the de-escalator of feeling. Natasha's withdrawals function symmetrically; when a conversation approaches her interior, she becomes operational, technical, professional. Both behaviors are tolerated because the group benefits from the off-ramp.

### 6.2.4 Devaluation (of Rampage, of "the common man" as a real category)

The team's defeat of Rampage in #5–6 is *narrated* as the suppression of a villain, never as the failure of their own mandate. The bankrupted small businessman in power-armor is precisely the demographic the Champions claim to exist for; treating him purely as a threat-to-be-subdued is a defensive devaluation that protects the team from having to revise its self-concept. Rampage's recurrence in #15–17 is the return of the repressed — and the team again responds by *fighting* him, never by *hearing* him.

### 6.2.5 Idealization (of Warren's money; of Hercules's mythic stature; of their own glamour)

The team idealizes its own most superficial assets. Warren's money is treated as if it constituted institutional legitimacy. Hercules's Olympian pedigree is treated as if it constituted command authority. The team's photogenic quality is treated as if it constituted public trust. Each is, in reality, brittle: money buys premises, not credentials; godhood confers strength, not strategy; glamour attracts cameras, not constituency. The idealizations hold the self-concept together precisely because they cannot be tested without breaking, and the team subtly avoids the tests.

### 6.2.6 Schizoid Fantasy (Warren's "West Coast" vision)

Warren's articulation of the Champions as a fundamentally different *kind* of super-team — democratic, accessible, of-the-people — is, on the evidence, a fantasy he sustains *in lieu of* relational engagement with his actual teammates. He cannot get Bobby to talk about losing the X-Men; he cannot get Natasha to discuss anything; he cannot reach Blaze through the Rider; he and Hercules speak past each other. So he builds, in his own head and in interviews, the *team-that-the-Champions-would-be-if-they-were-the-team-he-imagines*. The fantasy is a substitute relationship with the team itself.

---

## 6.3 NEUROTIC DEFENSES (Level 3 — Higher-Functioning Register)

Where the team manages to operate above the borderline register, it does so via these.

### 6.3.1 Intellectualization (Warren's mandate language)

The "for the common man" framing is itself an intellectualization: it converts the team's diffuse, undertheorized founding into a *concept* that can be discussed, defended, and printed on a press release. Concept-work substitutes for the harder labor of figuring out who, specifically, the team is *to each other*.

### 6.3.2 Rationalization (post-hoc mission selection)

The Champions take cases as they arrive — Pluto, the Stranger, Rampage, the Griffin, Swarm, the Sentinels, MODOK — and *rationalize* each as an expression of the mandate. None of these cases is "for the common man" in any operational sense; they are the standard rogues' gallery of any Marvel team. The post-hoc rationalization preserves the mandate without ever requiring the team to act on it.

### 6.3.3 Displacement (command friction redirected onto enemies)

Hercules and Natasha's unresolved command dispute is displaced, throughout the run, onto whichever villain is at hand. The intensity Hercules brings to combat with Pluto, with Typhon, with the Sentinels frequently overshoots the tactical requirement — it is the leadership-anxiety being discharged at a permissible target. Natasha's coldly precise dismantling of opponents reads, in the same frame, as the displaced exercise of the authority the team will not formally cede her.

### 6.3.4 Reaction Formation (the warmth of combat care)

The team's striking willingness to take damage for each other — well-documented across the middle issues of the run — is, in part, *reaction formation* against the off-duty distance. The team cannot sit in a room and ask each other how they are; the team can and will interpose a body between a teammate and a death-ray. The exaggerated combat-care compensates for the under-developed relational-care.

### 6.3.5 Isolation of Affect (Romanoff's operational register)

Natasha's professional manner — the clipped briefings, the analytic detachment, the absence of biographical disclosure — is the team's most polished isolation-of-affect defense. Her trauma history, her Red Room conditioning, her recent rupture with Murdock are all present in her behavior and absent from her speech. The team benefits: her competence is uncontaminated by her wounds, at the cost of her wounds going untreated.

---

## 6.4 "MATURE" DEFENSES (Level 4 — Where the Team Briefly Almost Functions)

The team does not have many of these. The few it has are the source of whatever genuine virtue the Champions accumulate.

### 6.4.1 Humor (Bobby's *other* register)

Iceman's humor is double-coded. As established above, it is often passive-aggressive deflation. But in a meaningful minority of instances — the post-victory beats, the late-night patrol banter with Warren — it operates as *genuine* mature humor: the metabolization of fear and absurdity into something the team can share. This is the closest the Champions come to spontaneous relational warmth that is not combat-mediated.

### 6.4.2 Sublimation (Warren's philanthropy as administrative work)

Warren's over-functioning — funding the headquarters, paying the staff, handling press, doing the unglamorous logistical labor — is a sublimation of his more chaotic affective material (the abandonment-residue of the X-Men's collapse, his unresolved feelings about his own wealth). It is the team's most consistently mature defense and its most exploited one; the entire group rides on Warren's sublimated anxiety, which is why funding collapse is the #1 pressure point identified in Section 5.

### 6.4.3 Altruism (genuine, in the field)

Where the team's mandate is performative, its in-field altruism toward civilians is sincere. Hercules's protectiveness of bystanders, Angel's rescue reflexes, Iceman's instinct to shield, Blaze's residual decency even under Zarathos's influence, Natasha's willingness to take the harder shot to spare a non-combatant — these are *real*. The altruism is the moral core that the team's structural deficits never quite destroy.

### 6.4.4 Anticipation (Romanoff, partially)

Of all the members, only Natasha is capable of anticipatory threat-modeling, and she exercises it inconsistently — sometimes saving the team, sometimes withholding the analysis. The defense is present in the group's stack only because she carries it; it does not propagate. When she leaves the room, the team becomes purely reactive.

**Notably absent from the mature stack:** *Suppression* (the conscious deferral of difficult feeling for later processing) is not in evidence; the team *re*-presses rather than suppresses, because there is no "later" in which the feelings will be addressed. *Sublimation* exists at Warren's level but is not group-shared.

---

## 6.5 POSITIVE COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS

Distinct from defenses (which manage anxiety) are compensations (which fill structural gaps). The team has several genuine ones.

- **Combat trust as relational currency.** The team's tactical chemistry by the middle of the run is real, hard-won, and operationally effective. It compensates for the absence of biographical intimacy by creating a different *kind* of intimacy — the somatic, wordless trust of bodies that have moved together under fire. This is not nothing. It is the team's most authentic accomplishment.
- **Distributed expertise.** Each member brings a non-overlapping skill: Hercules (raw power/myth-tier engagement), Natasha (espionage/tactics), Blaze (mystical/dissociative reach), Iceman (area-effect control), Angel (mobility/recon). The team is *functionally* well-composed even where it is *relationally* poorly composed. Compensates for the absence of doctrine by making improvisation viable.
- **Warren's infrastructure.** The premises, the staff, the public-relations apparatus. Compensates for the absence of institutional legitimacy by simulating it convincingly enough that the team can operate.
- **Mutual non-interference in private life.** A negative virtue that functions as a positive compensation. The team's off-duty distance, while pathological in attachment terms, also means that no member's individual life is *colonized* by the team. Each is free to maintain Roxanne, Iris, the X-Men, Olympus, the SHIELD residue — to keep their other anchors. The team is a port, not a home, and several members benefit from that limit.
- **Aesthetic coherence.** Costuming, branding, the West Coast aesthetic, the photogenic group composition. Trivial-seeming but operationally real: it gives the public something to recognize, which compensates for the team's lack of doctrinal articulation. The Champions are *visually legible* in a way that buys them time the substance does not earn.

---

## 6.6 STRUCTURAL / META-LEVEL DEFENSES

These operate at the level of the team's *form* rather than any single behavior.

### 6.6.1 The Roster as Defense

The roster itself is a defense against intimacy. Five members, each on a different scale of being, each with non-overlapping personal anchors, each with a built-in exit: Hercules can return to Olympus, Natasha to espionage, Blaze to stunt work or to the Rider's wanderings, Warren and Bobby to the X-Men. *Every member has a back door.* This is not accident; it is the unconscious selection criterion of a team that does not want to be permanent. A team that wanted permanence would have built convergent dependencies; the Champions built divergent ones.

### 6.6.2 The Mandate as Defense

"For the common man" is structurally vague enough to be unfalsifiable. No specific civilian constituency is named, no specific service is committed to, no specific metric of success is established. The mandate's vagueness is its defensive function: it cannot be failed because it cannot be measured. The single time it nearly is measured (Rampage) is the moment the team begins to come apart.

### 6.6.3 The Headquarters as Defense

The Los Angeles base is a *containment vessel* for the group's incoherence. By having premises, the team can point to a thing and call it *the Champions*, deferring the harder question of whether the *people* are a team. Real estate as identity-substitute.

### 6.6.4 Cancellation as Defense

The team's terminal defense — and the one that ultimately succeeds. The series ends mid-arc, the team dissolves without a decision-scene, and every survivor is freed from having to consciously *leave*. Cancellation, framed in-universe as the team simply *not continuing*, is the perfect avoidant exit: no member had to be the one who quit, no member had to be the one who was left. The group dissolved by *entropy*, which is the form of dissolution that requires the least psychological work from its participants. This is why the post-dissolution embarrassment is so uniform: each survivor knows, at some level, that they *let* the team end rather than ending it.

---

## 6.7 RANK-ORDERED DEFENSE INVENTORY (Most Primitive → Most Mature)

1. **Denial of formation conditions** — the team was not assembled, it was *interrupted into existence*; this fact is never acknowledged.
2. **Psychotic splitting of Blaze/Zarathos** — the Rider is not a teammate's condition, it is a weather event.
3. **Projective identification onto the Avengers** — our deficits are their character flaws.
4. **Acting out via mission tempo** — internal tension is anesthetized by external engagement.
5. **Somatization** — the body bleeds what the team cannot say.
6. **Passive aggression** (Bobby's deflective humor; Natasha's withdrawals) — feeling is exited through assigned roles.
7. **Devaluation of Rampage / of the mandate's test cases** — the people the mandate exists to serve are reclassified as threats when they fail to ratify the team's self-image.
8. **Idealization of money / godhood / glamour** — superficial assets stand in for substantive legitimacy.
9. **Schizoid fantasy** (Warren) — the team-as-imagined substitutes for the team-as-encountered.
10. **Intellectualization** — concept-work substitutes for relational labor.
11. **Rationalization** — mission selection retrofitted to mandate.
12. **Displacement** — command friction discharged through enemies.
13. **Reaction formation** — combat-care compensates for absent off-duty care.
14. **Isolation of affect** (Romanoff) — competence uncontaminated by wounds, wounds untreated.
15. **Humor** (Bobby's higher register) — occasional, real.
16. **Sublimation** (Warren's administrative labor) — chaos converted to logistics.
17. **Altruism** — sincere in the field, the moral core.
18. **Anticipation** (Romanoff, partial) — present but not propagated.

---

## 6.8 SYNTHESIS: WHAT THE DEFENSIVE STACK REVEALS

The Champions' defensive architecture is *bottom-heavy*. The team's working capital is concentrated in immature defenses (acting out, somatization, passive aggression, devaluation, idealization) with a thin and unevenly distributed mature layer carried almost entirely by two members (Warren's sublimation, Natasha's anticipation, Bobby's humor when it lands). The primitive defenses, while sparingly deployed, are operative precisely at the points where the team's *existence* is at stake — formation, mandate, the Ghost Rider problem — meaning the team's foundations rest on its most fragile psychic operations.

The positive compensations are real and they are what made the team *worth* the 17 issues: combat trust, distributed expertise, infrastructure, aesthetic legibility, the negative grace of non-interference. These are not trivial. A team can be built on these things, given time and intentionality. The Champions had neither.

The meta-level defenses — roster as escape-hatch, mandate as unfalsifiable, headquarters as identity-substitute, cancellation as exit — are the most diagnostically important. They reveal that the *form* of the team was, from the beginning, organized to permit its own dissolution. The Champions did not break because their defenses failed. The Champions broke because their defenses *worked*: they protected each member from the painful labor of staying, and so each member, when the structural prop was removed, was already free to leave.

The retrospective embarrassment of the survivors, then, has a precise referent. It is not embarrassment at the heroism (which was real), nor at the costumes (which were of their era), nor at the cases (which were standard). It is embarrassment at *how well the defenses worked* — at having participated in a team whose every psychic operation was, in retrospect, an elegant arrangement for not having to mean it.

— UATU, observing.


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# LONGITUDINAL PSYCHOLOGICAL PROFILE — THE CHAMPIONS (LOS ANGELES)

## Preliminary Note on Method

A team that operationally existed for ~24 in-universe months and 17 published issues (1975–1978) does not, on its face, support a "decade-by-decade" longitudinal frame. But the Champions are unusual: the *group-self* persisted long after the operational unit dissolved, carried forward as memory, embarrassment, retrospective construction, and intermittent flashback across every member's subsequent four decades of publication. The patient on the table is therefore not only the working team (1975–1978) but its *afterlife as an internal object* in each surviving member's psychology — what attachment theorists would call the **internal working model of the Champions-experience**, which continues to organize each member's subsequent team affiliations. This profile tracks both: the brief somatic life of the unit, and the long psychic life of its ghost.

Frameworks applied: Bowlby/Ainsworth attachment categories at the group level; Bion's basic-assumption group dynamics; Tuckman's forming-storming-norming-performing-adjourning (with adjourning as the operative phase the team never properly executed); Marcia's identity-status model (foreclosure vs. moratorium vs. diffusion vs. achievement); Edmondson on psychological safety; Boss on ambiguous loss; Linehan on emotion dysregulation translated to group affect; and the organizational-development literature on post-mortem grief in disbanded units.

---

## ERA I — GESTATION AND PRE-FORMATION (the months preceding *Champions* #1)

**Affect regulation:** does not exist *as a group*. There is no group. There are five separately-dysregulated individuals converging on Los Angeles, each running a private and incompatible affect-management protocol. Romanoff is in flat-affect post-rupture withdrawal following the Murdock separation (carried over from *Daredevil* #124 territory). Warren is in compensatory hyper-functioning, having converted X-Men dissolution into administrative busyness around his fortune and his westward relocation. Bobby is in adolescent-adjacent jocularity covering depressive features — the X-Men have stopped being his holding environment and he is, functionally, a sophomore with superpowers and nowhere to put them. Blaze is in chronic dissociative readiness, white-knuckling Zarathos between stunt gigs. Hercules is in one of his recurrent dysphoric exiles from Olympus, self-medicating with wine and grandiosity.

**Cognitive style (pre-group):** five non-overlapping cognitive frames. There is no shared epistemology because there is no shared anything.

**Self-concept (pre-group):** each member is in *identity moratorium* in Marcia's sense — actively exploring without commitment. This is the single most important pre-existing condition. Five people in moratorium will not produce a team in identity-achievement; they will produce a team in **identity foreclosure**, because the first available shared label will be grabbed and ratified without the work.

**Diagnostic flag:** the group is born into a maximally vulnerable substrate. Every member is in a transitional affective state with reduced defenses, and a group formed under these conditions will inherit the unprocessed material of all five.

---

## ERA II — ACUTE FORMATION (*Champions* #1–4, the Olympian assault and immediate aftermath)

**Affect regulation:** *trauma-bonded coregulation*. The team's first shared experience is being attacked, and the regulatory mechanism that emerges is **mutual deployment as anxiolytic** — fighting together discharges the cortisol of being separately heartbroken. This is observable as an almost euphoric tactical chemistry in the early issues that is disproportionate to how long the members have known each other. In attachment terms, this is the **fear-conditioned proximity-seeking** that Bowlby identified as the most rapid (and most brittle) bond-forming mechanism. The team learns within days that its own collective body produces relief from individual distress *when threatened* and does nothing of the kind *when not*.

**Cognitive style:** intensely present-tense, threat-focused, low-elevation. The cognitive aperture during formation is so narrow it cannot conceive of "next month." This is normatively appropriate to acute threat response and pathologically persistent thereafter.

**Self-concept:** identity foreclosure executed cleanly by issue #3. The label "Champions" and Warren's mandate are accepted *because* they are available, not because they are negotiated. Marcia would call this textbook foreclosure: identity commitment without exploration. Foreclosure-status identities are stable on the surface and catastrophically fragile under value-challenge, because no internal warrant for the identity has been generated. This precisely predicts the team's later collapse under Rampage-class moral challenges.

**Group attachment classification (Ainsworth analog):** **disorganized-with-anxious-features**. The team simultaneously seeks proximity (cohesion in combat) and cannot tolerate it (distance between missions), with no coherent strategy — the hallmark of disorganized attachment.

---

## ERA III — OPERATIONAL ADOLESCENCE (*Champions* #5–11, the middle run)

**Affect regulation:** matures *only along the threat-axis*. The team becomes genuinely good at co-regulating under fire — by issue #10 the tactical hand-offs (Iceman platforms for Angel's strafing runs, Romanoff's terminal target-prioritization, Hercules as anchor, Blaze as wild-card disruptor) read as a unit that has integrated. Off-axis, affect regulation *regresses*. Between missions the team is, if anything, more uncomfortable with itself than at formation, because the contrast between in-combat closeness and off-duty distance becomes legible to the members and is unspeakable. This is the **paradox of fight-flight cohesion** in Bion's terms: the better the group gets at fighting, the more it requires fighting to feel coherent, which becomes a self-reinforcing loop.

**Cognitive style:** development of a *team-level cognitive bifurcation*. The unit develops two parallel cognitive registers: a high-functioning tactical register (shared, fluent, mostly nonverbal, distributed across all five) and a degraded strategic register (un-shared, never fluent, defaulted to Warren-as-administrator and Hercules-as-figurehead). This bifurcation is observable in Edmondson-style psychological-safety markers: the team will dissent freely about fields of fire and ice-slide angles; it will not dissent at all about mission selection or mandate. Members who dissent strategically (occasional Romanoff demurrals) are absorbed by deflection, not engaged.

**Self-concept:** the first cracks appear. The Rampage arc (#5–6) delivers the team its first sustained encounter with the failure-mode of its own mandate — the literal common man recoded by trauma as their enemy — and the team's response is to *not metabolize it*. This is the period in which the foreclosed identity begins generating low-grade cognitive dissonance that the group has no procedure for resolving. Warren over-functions further to absorb the dissonance administratively. Romanoff withdraws further to absorb it diagnostically (she sees the problem and cannot fix it from her position in the chain of command). Hercules drinks more.

**Stress-response innovation:** the team develops the **mission-as-displacement** habit in this era. When internal tension rises, someone (usually Warren or Hercules) finds a fight. This is the precise group analog of behavioral activation deployed as avoidance — productive on the surface, hollowing under.

**Onboarding pathology:** Darkstar's frictionless absorption in #7 occurs in this era and is the cleanest data point for the team's complete absence of identity-defense mechanisms. A team with a coherent self-concept *vets* additions. The Champions cannot vet because they do not know what they are admitting people into.

---

## ERA IV — TERMINAL PHASE AND NON-ADJOURNMENT (*Champions* #12–17, dissolution by cancellation)

**Affect regulation:** decompensation. The combat-cohesion regulator that had carried the team through Era III begins to fray under sustained, complex pressure (the Sentinels/Stranger arc, MODOK, the resurgent Rampage). Tactical hand-offs that had been fluent in Era III become clunky as members start operating as parallel soloists sharing a battlefield rather than as an integrated unit. The team is regressing toward its pre-formation state under load.

**Cognitive style:** complete strategic abdication. There is no long-horizon planning in this era at all. The strategic register collapses entirely; Warren ceases to over-function (the financial and emotional cost has become unrecoverable) and no one replaces him. The team is, in this era, *only* tactical.

**Self-concept:** identity diffusion supervenes on the prior foreclosure. The team can no longer answer "what are the Champions?" even at the level of rote mandate-recital. The label persists; the content is gone.

**Adjournment failure (the central pathology of this era).** Tuckman's group-development model identifies *adjourning* as the final, necessary phase of any bounded team — the deliberate ritualized work of ending well: acknowledgment of contribution, articulation of what was learned, blessing of dispersal. The Champions never adjourn. The book is cancelled mid-arc; the team dissolves by entropy, not by decision. **No one fights for the team to continue, and no one fights for the team to end with honor.** This is the single most consequential fact in the team's entire psychic history, because the absence of an adjournment ritual converts the dissolution into what Pauline Boss calls **ambiguous loss** — a relationship that has ended without ending, that persists as an unmetabolized internal object. Every subsequent era of every member's afterlife is shaped by this failure.

---

## ERA V — IMMEDIATE POST-DISSOLUTION (months 1–24 after the team ends)

The unit no longer exists operationally but the *group-self* is now an active internal object in five separate psychologies, and it begins behaving like one.

**Affect regulation (in the internal object):** members report — through subsequent appearances and reflective moments in their solo runs — a low-grade dysphoric residue when the Champions are mentioned. This is not guilt or grief in pure form; it is the affect signature of ambiguous loss: a flat, slightly nauseated, mildly defensive avoidance. The internal object is *uncomfortable to touch* and is therefore not touched.

**Cognitive style (in the internal object):** rationalization and dismissal. Each member, when narrating their own arc, *minimizes* the Champions period. Warren classifies it as a youthful misadventure. Romanoff codes it as a wilderness year between more legible chapters. Bobby barely references it. This minimization is the cognitive defense that allows the affect signature to remain unprocessed: if the period did not really matter, the failure to adjourn does not need to be addressed.

**Self-concept (in the internal object):** the team's death without ceremony leaves each member with a small, unintegrated identity-fragment — the *Champions-self* — that does not fit cleanly into their pre- or post-Champions identity narratives. This fragment is what surfaces as the embarrassment-signature in later interviews and reflective beats. It is not shame about specific acts; it is the discomfort of carrying a self-component that was never validated by completion.

---

## ERA VI — THE EXTENDED MIDDLE PERIOD (roughly the decade after dissolution, across each member's continuing publication)

This is the era in which the Champions-experience becomes a **structural variable in each member's subsequent team selections**, observable across canon.

- **Warren** moves through Defenders affiliations and into X-Factor, and his subsequent team behavior is marked by a refusal to fund-and-found in the Champions mode. He never again writes the check for a team he has not vetted. The Apocalypse/Death period that begins in this era can be read in part as a *catastrophic regression past* the Champions-experience into a more primary trauma; the Champions-self is not addressed, it is buried under a larger psychic event.

- **Romanoff** returns to Avengers and intelligence-affiliated work, and her subsequent team behavior is marked by an absolute insistence on chain-of-command clarity and on vetting. The Darkstar lapse is *the* lapse she does not repeat. Her leadership style across the Secret Avengers era and after carries the negative imprint of the Champions: she does the strategic work she did not do then.

- **Bobby** drifts. The Champions period sits inside his longer arc of *not developing*, and the unprocessed adjournment-failure is one strand of the broader stagnation that critics and characters alike identify in him through the 1980s. He does not internalize a corrective.

- **Blaze** returns to itinerancy. The team-experience is one of several attempted holding environments that did not hold him; the lesson he draws is that his condition is incompatible with affiliation, which is partially right and entirely defensive.

- **Hercules** continues his oscillation between Olympian and Avenger contexts; the Champions register as one more brief mortal entanglement in a centuries-long pattern and are essentially absorbed by his longer narrative rhythm.

**Affect at the group-internal-object level in this era:** stabilized as *low-grade aversive nostalgia*. The Champions become, for the survivors, a memory category one does not visit but cannot quite throw away — psychologically analogous to a box of college photographs from a relationship that ended badly.

**Cognitive style at the group-internal-object level:** consolidated minimization. The team's narrative footprint shrinks in each member's self-told story. This is adaptive in the short run and corrosive in the long run because it precludes the integration that would resolve the ambiguous loss.

---

## ERA VII — LATE MIDDLE PERIOD (1990s–2000s publication, in-universe roughly a decade further on)

**Affect regulation:** the internal object becomes inert for most members. Time has done what adjournment ritual would have done faster and cleaner — the affect signature has flattened to the point that the Champions period is recallable without significant distress. This is not resolution; it is **erosion of affective charge through non-use**, which leaves the cognitive structure intact but emotionally inactive. The internal object is now scar tissue rather than wound.

**Cognitive style:** the team is now narratable as anecdote. Members who reference the Champions in this era do so with the conversational ease of distance, but the content of the reference is consistently *reductive* — the period is summarized rather than examined. The strategic register that the team failed to develop in life is also absent in its members' retrospective accounts: no one extracts a lesson, articulates a model, or carries a doctrine forward. This is the cognitive footprint of unprocessed experience: it remains *episodic* and never becomes *semantic*.

**Self-concept:** the Champions-fragment in each member's identity has been encapsulated rather than integrated — walled off as a chapter that happened, not metabolized as a chapter that *means*.

---

## ERA VIII — LATE PUBLICATION ERA (2000s–present, 30+ years out)

**Affect regulation:** the internal object is now functionally archival. Flashback appearances (*Avengers Forever*, *Marvel Team-Up* legacy beats, nostalgia issues) treat the Champions with the bemused affection reserved for embarrassing but harmless past selves. The affective signature is identifiable but minimal.

**Cognitive style:** crystallized into a stable, slightly self-deprecating *story* — a small set of standard beats (we tried, we were photogenic, it did not work, we moved on) that members will produce on demand. This is the cognitive fate of any experience that is encapsulated rather than integrated: it becomes a *script*, and the script substitutes for the memory.

**Self-concept:** the Champions-fragment has now been so long encapsulated that it functions as part of each member's history-of-selves rather than as live identity material. The members are at peace with the period in the specific sense that nothing about it is currently demanding.

**But the structural deficit persists.** The lesson the team failed to learn — *that you cannot run a unit on rebound attachment, foreclosed identity, and combat-cohesion alone* — was never explicitly extracted, and so it must be re-learned (and is re-learned, partially, by successive teams the survivors join). The reasonably-good outcomes of those subsequent teams represent procedural learning rather than insight: the survivors behave differently without having articulated *why*. This is the long signature of unprocessed group trauma — corrected behavior without integrated understanding.

---

## CROSS-ERA SYNTHESIS

**Affect regulation arc:** acute trauma-bonded coregulation (Era II) → bifurcated regulation, in-combat fluent and off-duty failing (Era III) → decompensation (Era IV) → ambiguous-loss dysphoria (Era V) → aversive nostalgia (Era VI) → erosion to inertness (Era VII) → archival stability (Era VIII). The arc is the standard trajectory of an *unmourned* attachment: not resolution, but the slow draining of affective charge from an unprocessed loss.

**Cognitive style arc:** narrow, present-tense, threat-focused throughout the operational life (Eras II–IV), with no maturation of the strategic register; minimization (Era V) → consolidated minimization (Era VI) → episodic-not-semantic recall (Era VII) → crystallized script (Era VIII). The cognitive arc is the signature of an experience that was never properly *thought about* — it has been managed, not understood.

**Self-concept arc:** moratorium (Era I) → foreclosure (Era II) → strained foreclosure under dissonance (Era III) → diffusion (Era IV) → unintegrated fragment (Era V) → encapsulated fragment (Eras VI–VII) → archival fragment (Era VIII). The team never moved from foreclosure to achievement, which is the identity-developmental task it was structurally incapable of completing in 17 issues.

**The central longitudinal finding:** the Champions are a study in what happens when a group is allowed to *not finish*. Every subsequent psychological signature in every surviving member's relationship to the team is a consequence of the failure to adjourn. The dissolution-by-cancellation is not just a publishing fact; it is, when read into the diegesis, the determinative event in the team's psychic life. A team that ends without ceremony does not stop existing — it converts into an internal object that each member carries, unprocessed, for the remainder of their published life, and the cost of that conversion is the slow encapsulation of a self-fragment that could have been integrated had anyone, at the end, said: *this is what we were, this is what we learned, this is how we let it go.*

No one said it. The fragment remains.

— UATU, observing across the decades.


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL — THE CHAMPIONS (Los Angeles, Original Roster)

*Patient: a five-body group organism, intake date c. October 1975, terminus c. January 1978, total contact period ~27 in-universe months. Assessment conducted retrospectively from complete behavioral record (Champions #1–17, ancillary appearances, and post-dissolution member testimony). All diagnostic language uses DSM-5-TR and ICD-11 analogs adapted to group-level psychiatry (Bion, Yalom, Edmondson, Hopper, Tuckman).*

---

## I. PRESENTING COMPLAINT

The group presents — or rather, is presented by its own behavioral record — with a constellation of complaints that no individual member would have brought to clinical attention, because the group never developed the meta-cognitive capacity to recognize itself as a patient. Symptoms emerge only on third-party review: inability to function except under acute external stimulus; recurrent oscillation between fused combat-identity and dissociated off-duty drift; chronic inability to articulate shared purpose; recurrent failure to learn from feedback (the Rampage cycle); progressive command erosion; and terminal entropic dissolution without precipitating event. The chief complaint, were the group capable of voicing one, would be: *we cannot tell whether we exist when no one is shooting at us.*

---

## II. WORKING DIAGNOSIS (PRIMARY)

### Bion Basic-Assumption Group, Fight-Flight Subtype, with Secondary Dependency Features, in Failed Work-Group Formation (Chronic, Moderate Severity)

This is the spine diagnosis. Bion's framework — the indispensable nosology for group-level psychiatry — distinguishes the *Work Group* (oriented to task, capable of reality-testing, able to tolerate frustration and uncertainty) from three regressive *Basic Assumption* states into which groups collapse when work anxiety exceeds capacity: **Dependency** (the group orbits an idealized leader expected to magically provide), **Fight-Flight** (the group can only organize around an external enemy or escape from one), and **Pairing** (the group invests hope in a generative dyad that will produce a savior).

The Champions are a near-textbook **Fight-Flight** presentation with **Dependency** comorbidity. Diagnostic criteria, all met:

**A. Group exists in functional terms only in the presence of an external threat.** Of the 17 issues, approximately 14 open with the team already mobilized against an active adversary or mobilizing within the first three pages. The remaining issues — interstitial breathers — show the group in marked dysfunction: aimless conversation, low-affect interaction, members peeling off into solo subplots. The group has no demonstrated capacity for non-threat-organized productive activity.

**B. Internal aggression is consistently externalized.** Hercules/Romanoff command friction never resolves through negotiation; it is *displaced* onto the next opponent, where Hercules's bid for dominance can be reframed as heroic initiative and Romanoff's competence as tactical assist. The group does not have intra-group conflict resolution mechanisms; it has *targets*.

**C. Dependency features clustering on two members.** Warren is the dependency object for *infrastructure* (the group fantasizes that money solves the team's existential problems; it does not). Hercules is the dependency object for *presence* (the group fantasizes that mythic gravitas confers institutional legitimacy; it does not). Both objects are inadequate to the projection. Warren is twenty-something and untrained as an executive; Hercules is, in clinical terms, a chronically intoxicated demigod with poor frustration tolerance. The dependency objects buckle under the projection, which the group does not metabolize.

**D. Failure of Work-Group emergence is *complete*, not partial.** A struggling Work Group will at minimum convene regular task-oriented meetings, attempt agenda-setting, and produce documentary artifacts (rosters, protocols, after-action reviews). The Champions produce none of these. Warren handles administrative matters unilaterally and off-page. The group never holds a single on-panel meeting that could be classified as Work-Group functioning under Bion's criteria.

**Severity rating: moderate.** The group is not psychotic-equivalent (no shared delusion, no break with consensus reality). It is not malignant (no harm-doing as group purpose). It is *structurally non-viable* — a moderate severity finding because the dysfunction is pervasive across functional domains but does not produce acute decompensation; it produces slow attrition culminating in dissolution.

---

## III. CO-OCCURRING DIAGNOSES (COMORBIDITY)

### 1. Group-Level Adjustment Disorder with Mixed Anxiety and Depressed Mood (F43.23 analog), Acute at Formation, Chronic Over Course

DSM-5-TR criteria for Adjustment Disorder require (a) emotional or behavioral symptoms in response to identifiable stressor(s), (b) within three months of onset, (c) clinically significant, and (d) not better explained by another disorder or normative bereavement. Adapted to group level:

- **Identifiable stressor:** every founding member arrives in a state of fresh attachment rupture. Romanoff's separation from Murdock is weeks old. Worthington and Drake are processing the original X-Men's dissolution and Professor Xavier's effective absence. Blaze is alienated from his Quentin Carnival/Hollywood milieu. Hercules is in a fresh exile from Olympus, the latest in a recurring pattern. The *group itself* is a coping mechanism convened by five people in concurrent acute-loss states.
- **Onset:** symptomatic from day one. The group never has a non-symptomatic baseline against which to measure deterioration.
- **Clinical significance:** demonstrated by operational impairment, identity diffusion, and ultimately dissolution.
- **Not better explained by bereavement:** the losses are real but the group's mode of responding — fusion-by-crisis without grief work — is pathological, not normative.

The diagnosis becomes **chronic** (specifier: persistent, >6 months) by issue #6 and never remits.

### 2. Low Psychological Safety (Edmondson framework; not a DSM entity but a validated organizational-psychiatry construct)

Edmondson defines psychological safety as the shared belief that the team is safe for interpersonal risk-taking — that one can voice dissent, admit error, ask naïve questions, or surface bad news without status loss. The Champions score floor-level on every Edmondson indicator:

- **No on-panel admission of error** by any member regarding team-level decisions. Individual members admit personal mistakes (Blaze about Zarathos, Drake about youth); no one ever says "the team made the wrong call."
- **No naïve questions asked.** The most diagnostically important silence in the entire run: nobody ever asks, in plain language, *"What are we for?"* The question is unaskable because the absence of an answer is unbearable.
- **Bad news is suppressed.** The Rampage feedback — that the team's signature villain is a literal embodiment of the demographic it claims to serve — is never surfaced as a strategic problem. It is treated as a recurring fight, not a referendum.
- **Dissent is routed through performance, not voice.** Romanoff's disagreement with Hercules manifests as superior battlefield execution, not as conversation. Warren's anxieties about the mission manifest as more spending, not as renegotiation.

### 3. Group Identity Diffusion (Erikson/Kernberg analog applied to group selfhood)

Kernberg's identity diffusion construct — internally contradictory, poorly integrated self-representations, with corresponding inability to form stable representations of others — maps onto the Champions with unusual cleanness. Asked "who are the Champions," the group will produce at least five non-overlapping answers:

- Warren: *a publicly accountable West Coast super-team for ordinary people.*
- Romanoff: *a working unit I happen to belong to while between attachments.*
- Hercules: *a band of mortal companions doing honor to my presence.*
- Blaze: *somewhere I can be useful without burning anything important down.*
- Drake: *the X-Men, sort of, but warmer, and with Warren.*

These are not five facets of one identity. They are five different organizations sharing a roster. Identity diffusion is the technical name for this.

### 4. Hopper's "Fourth Basic Assumption" — Incohesion: Aggregation/Massification (I:A/M)

Earl Hopper's expansion of Bion identifies a fourth basic-assumption state characterized by oscillation between *Aggregation* (members behave as isolated atoms, no group feeling) and *Massification* (members fuse into undifferentiated mass with loss of individual judgment). The Champions exhibit textbook I:A/M oscillation: between missions they are an *aggregate* (five solo operators sharing an address), during missions they are a *mass* (tactical fusion with suspension of individual deliberation). They never occupy the middle ground — *cohesion proper*, in which individuated members maintain differentiation while sustaining group feeling. The whipsaw between aggregation and massification, with no intermediate cohesion, is itself diagnostic of group-level trauma response (Hopper traces I:A/M to collective traumatic experience; the Champions' substrate of concurrent recent loss qualifies).

### 5. Member-Level Untreated Conditions Affecting Group Function

The group does not have a body, but it inherits the untreated conditions of its members, which become group-level operational risks:

- **Blaze's chronic dissociative state** (Zarathos possession) is, individually, a candidate for Dissociative Identity Disorder with significant impairment; at group level it is an *unscheduled tactical liability with no containment protocol*. The group's failure to develop a protocol is a group-psychiatric finding, distinct from Blaze's personal diagnosis.
- **Romanoff's complex-trauma profile** (Red Room conditioning, prior pharmacological manipulation, attachment ruptures across her romantic history) is unshared and unmetabolized. Her trauma-informed wariness pervades her command behavior but is never legible to teammates as such, producing repeated misattribution (Hercules reads her caution as disrespect; Drake reads it as coolness).
- **Hercules's alcohol-use behavior** at a volume that would be incapacitating in any non-Olympian normalizes intoxication as a team-leadership condition. The group does not have a sober chain of command at any point in the run.
- **Worthington's incipient mood instability** (which will, in later canon, surface dramatically) is in subclinical form during the Champions period but contributes to his over-functioning administrative pattern as defensive structure.
- **Drake's identity foreclosure** (still configured as the X-Men's youngest, performing adolescence into his twenties) limits his capacity to occupy adult roles within the team and contributes to the failure of generational/role differentiation.

None of these member conditions is the group's diagnosis. All of them are inputs to the group's diagnosis.

---

## IV. ETIOLOGY

Group-level psychiatric formulation requires answering three etiological questions: *why did this group form, why did it form this way, and why did the dysfunction persist?*

**Why it formed:** the group did not form by deliberation. It accreted under fire, at a single geographic point (UCLA campus), during a coordinated mythic assault. Etiologically this is critical: the founding condition was *external coercion by threat*, not *internal convergence by purpose*. Groups born under external coercion typically require subsequent purpose-finding work to stabilize as Work Groups. The Champions never performed this work.

**Why it formed this way:** the five members were maximally available to bonding-under-threat because each was in attachment crisis. Acute loss states produce elevated bonding receptivity (well documented in the disaster-psychiatry literature on "trauma bonding" and the post-bereavement attachment literature). The combination of (a) external coercive event, (b) five concurrent acute-loss states, and (c) physical co-location produced a group whose binding agent was *shared availability for rebound*, not *shared purpose, shared values, or shared method*. This is the etiological lesion.

**Why dysfunction persisted:** three reinforcing loops.

- *Combat reinforcement loop:* every successful mission reinforced the (correct) belief that the group works under fire, which reinforced the (incorrect) inference that the group works *as such*. The behavioral evidence the group accumulated was selectively combat-positive; off-duty dysfunction was attributed to circumstance rather than structure.
- *Funding insulation loop:* Warren's wealth removed the normal pressures (rent, salary, equipment costs) that force ordinary organizations into governance development. The Champions never had to professionalize because they never had to budget. Resource insulation is a known suppressor of organizational maturation.
- *Mandate vagueness loop:* the "for the common man" mandate was sufficiently vague that no mission could clearly falsify it, which meant no feedback could compel revision. Unfalsifiable mission statements are organizationally pathognomonic; they preserve the appearance of purpose while preventing the work of purpose-finding.

---

## V. SYMPTOM PRESENTATION IN BEHAVIOR

A diagnosis is empty without symptom-to-behavior mapping. The following are the observable behavioral signatures of the diagnostic constellation:

**Symptom 1: Inability to convene a non-operational meeting.** Across 17 issues, there is no scene of the Champions sitting down, agenda in hand, to deliberate organizational matters. The closest analogs are Warren delivering executive announcements (premises, funding) which the others receive without amendment. This is a *negative* behavioral finding — symptomatic by absence.

**Symptom 2: Identity inconsistency across press interactions.** In every issue where members are interviewed, photographed, or addressed by civilians as Champions, the framing of the team varies by which member is speaking. The group has no shared script. Hercules will speak in mythic register; Warren will speak in civic register; Romanoff will deflect; Blaze will mumble; Drake will joke. The group has no spokesperson because there is nothing coherent to speak for.

**Symptom 3: Conflict-avoidance routing.** When intra-group tension rises, the *next panel* is reliably an external interruption — a villain attack, a news bulletin, a summons. The group's narrative rhythm is, on close reading, structured to interrupt every emergent intra-group conversation. This is not coincidence; it is the group's avoidance mechanism instantiated in the form of the book itself.

**Symptom 4: Failure to integrate feedback (Rampage cycle).** The Rampage encounters are the cleanest available natural experiment. A villain who is *categorically* the team's stated constituency returns repeatedly, radicalized by each engagement, and the team's tactics and self-understanding do not adjust between encounters. This is the symptomatic correlate of low psychological safety: the feedback exists, no member has standing to raise it, the lesson is not learned.

**Symptom 5: Onboarding without vetting (Darkstar).** A KGB-aligned defector is integrated within a single issue, with no security review, despite the team containing a former Soviet illegal who knows exactly what such a review should look like. The symptom is the *abdication* of Romanoff's professional knowledge — a group-level suppression of expertise that the group needs and has, but cannot tolerate using, because using it would require admitting institutional standing.

**Symptom 6: Terminal entropic dissolution.** The team does not vote to disband; it does not have a precipitating crisis that ends it; it does not even have a graceful sunset arc. It stops, mid-arc, because no one fights for its continuation. This is the behavioral correlate of identity diffusion: an entity that cannot articulate why it exists cannot mount a defense for continuing to exist.

**Symptom 7: Post-dissolution disavowal.** Members refer back to the period with embarrassment (Warren), silence (Hercules, Blaze), or wilderness-year framing (Romanoff, Drake). This collective amnesia is symptomatic. Healthy group experience is integrated and referenced; the Champions are scar tissue, dissociated from the members' integrated life narratives.

---

## VI. COURSE OVER TIME

**Phase 1, Acute Formation (issues #1–3, ~weeks 1–8):** flooding of new-group cohesion energy ("forming" in Tuckman's stage model, compressed atypically into combat). Group experiences itself as exhilarated and capable. Subjective: euphoric. Objective: pathologically rapid bonding without negotiation of norms.

**Phase 2, Norming Failure (issues #4–7, ~months 2–5):** the period in which a Work Group would establish norms, roles, and decision procedures. The Champions instead route into a Hercules/Romanoff command dispute that is never resolved, accept Warren's infrastructure decisions without deliberation, and admit Darkstar without vetting. Tuckman's "storming" and "norming" stages both fail. Group skips to performing.

**Phase 3, Operational Performance Without Structure (issues #8–13, ~months 6–14):** the group's apparent peak. Combat tactics are sharp; mutual trust under fire is real. To external observers and to the group itself, this looks like success. Diagnostically it is the *plateau before drift*, in which structural deficiencies are masked by tactical competence.

**Phase 4, Sustained Pressure and Fragmentation (issues #14–17, ~months 15–24):** under Sentinels/Stranger-arc pressure, the team begins to function as parallel solo operators sharing a battlefield. Command coherence visibly degrades. Members increasingly pursue personal subplots. Group identity, never strong, thins to nothing.

**Phase 5, Dissolution (~month 24–27):** the group ceases. There is no terminal event. The book ends mid-arc, which is the behavioral correlate of the diagnostic prediction: groups in the Champions' constellation dissolve by entropy because they have no internal mechanism to mobilize for continuation.

**Long-tail course:** post-dissolution, members revert to pre-Champions baselines or accelerate to subsequent affiliations (Romanoff to Avengers; Warren and Drake to X-Factor; Hercules to Avengers and Olympian arcs; Blaze to solo Ghost Rider material). No member experiences the Champions period as formative in a way they refer back to constructively. The group leaves no internalized "Champions self-state" in its members. This is the long-tail symptom: a group experience that produces no enduring identification in its participants is, by definition, a group that did not psychologically exist as a group.

---

## VII. DIFFERENTIAL DIAGNOSIS — WHAT THE CHAMPIONS ARE NOT

Rigorous psychiatric formulation requires explicit rule-outs. Each of the following is a diagnosis the Champions might superficially resemble and which must be excluded with reasoning.

### Rule-Out 1: Cult / High-Demand Group

Cult formations require (a) a charismatic ideologue with unfalsifiable doctrine, (b) in-group/out-group epistemology with thought-reform pressure, (c) escalating commitment mechanisms, (d) sanctions against exit. The Champions have *none* of these. Warren has money but not doctrine; Hercules has presence but not ideology. There is no in-group epistemology — members openly maintain external relationships, careers, and affiliations. There are no escalating commitments — the group does not extract increasing investment over time. Exit is unsanctioned; when members leave, no one pursues. *Ruled out.*

### Rule-Out 2: Paramilitary Organization

Paramilitary diagnosis requires chain of command, standard operating procedures, formal doctrine, training cycles, and accountability mechanisms. The Champions have a *contested* command (Hercules/Romanoff unresolved), *no* SOPs (each mission improvised), *no* doctrine ("for the common man" is a slogan, not doctrine), *no* training cycles, and *no* accountability mechanisms. Romanoff alone could impose paramilitary structure; her conspicuous failure to do so is itself diagnostic — she does not regard the unit as salvageable for that purpose. *Ruled out.*

### Rule-Out 3: Family System (e.g., Fantastic Four, X-Men)

Family-system diagnosis requires generational structure (parental figures who actually parent), sibling matrices with shared history, and the operation of family-of-origin dynamics in the present (replay of childhood roles, scapegoating, parentification). The Champions attempt a familial register — Warren and Drake import it from their X-Men experience — but it does not take. There are no parental figures (Hercules is *not* paternal; he is fraternal-with-rank-pretension). There is no shared history pre-formation. The familial transference does not stabilize. *Ruled out as primary*, though familial echoes from members' prior groups (X-Men for Warren/Drake) contribute to the dependency features.

### Rule-Out 4: Peer Collective / Non-Team (e.g., the Defenders)

Peer-collective diagnosis requires explicit refusal of team-form: no name as binding commitment, no public mandate, no infrastructure, ad-hoc convening only. The Defenders are the genre's reference case. The Champions are the *inverse*: they assert team-form publicly and contractually (name, press conferences, premises, funding) without doing the underlying work. They are a team that *performs* team-ness it has not earned, which is the opposite of the Defenders' refusal to perform team-ness they could have earned. *Ruled out.*

### Rule-Out 5: Startup / Founding-Team Dynamics

Superficially, the Champions resemble a startup: small founding team, charismatic capital source, public mission, growth aspirations. Startup-team dysfunctions (founder conflict, mission drift, premature scaling) do appear. But the Champions are not a startup because they lack the *metabolic feature* of startups: response to market feedback. A startup that ignored its primary customer signal (Rampage) for 17 issues would be insolvent in two; the Champions are insulated from feedback by Warren's wealth. The startup analogy fails at the feedback-loop level. *Ruled out as primary frame*; some founding-team features are real but secondary.

### Rule-Out 6: Group Psychosis / Folie à Plusieurs

Shared psychotic disorder requires a shared delusion, typically transmitted from a dominant member to suggestible others. The Champions have no shared delusion. Their mandate is not delusional; it is *aspirational and under-implemented*, which is a different category. No member exhibits psychotic features that could serve as the source. Reality-testing is intact across the group. *Ruled out.*

### Rule-Out 7: Major Group-Depressive Episode

A depressive presentation at group level would require pervasive anhedonia, loss of group energy, suicidal ideation analog (active wish for dissolution). The Champions are not depressed in operational hours; they are vivid, energetic, combat-engaged. Off-duty drift resembles depressive flattening but is better accounted for by the basic-assumption Fight-Flight framework: the group has no off-duty mode because the group has no non-threat purpose. The flatness is *structural*, not mood-disordered. *Ruled out as


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS — THE CHAMPIONS (Los Angeles, Original Roster)

*A condition-by-condition catalog of the group organism's tells, tics, micro-routines, and decision habits, derived from the seventeen-issue run and adjacent appearances. Where individual members produce a tell, it is logged as a team-level signal — the Atlas tracks how the *unit* behaves, including the predictable solo behaviors that constitute the team's collective signature.*

---

## I. CALM / BASELINE (Between Missions, Headquarters, Daylight Hours)

The Champions at rest are the Champions at their most revealing, because at rest they are barely a team at all. The headquarters — the leased high-rise office above Sunset, after the LA Coliseum debacle — is occupied unevenly. On any given weekday afternoon the file would log: Warren present (almost always), Bobby present (frequently, by Warren-gravity), Natasha intermittent, Hercules present-when-bored, Blaze rarely.

**Spatial habits.** The team has no shared common room they actually use. Warren works in the office proper; Bobby drifts to whatever room has a television; Hercules occupies the largest chair in any space he enters and tilts it backward until it creaks; Natasha takes the chair nearest an exit and with sightlines to two doors — a Red Room habit she has never decommissioned; Blaze, when present, stands rather than sits and positions himself near a window, because windows are egress for a man who occasionally combusts.

**Conversational tempo.** Slow, glancing, low-stakes. The Champions at baseline make small talk about the city, the weather, the press; they do not make small talk about themselves. Warren initiates roughly 60% of conversations. Hercules interrupts roughly 40% of them with a tangential anecdote from antiquity. Natasha contributes in clipped, accurate sentences and never volunteers a topic. Bobby cracks jokes at a rate of approximately one per ninety seconds — a measurable nervous-system tell, not humor. Blaze answers when asked and does not elaborate.

**Personal-maintenance routines logged.**
- Hercules: morning workout in the Coliseum or, post-relocation, the office gym; consumes wine from mid-afternoon onward; naps in the largest chair around 3 PM with mouth open; wakes refreshed and theatrical.
- Warren: arrives early, reviews team finances and press clippings, takes a flight circuit over the Pacific most mornings before dawn (observable by witnesses on the Santa Monica coast); shaves twice daily; changes shirts when sweat-stained.
- Bobby: arrives late, eats constantly (high-caloric load is a real metabolic need given his cryokinetic burn rate, but the *form* is teenage — burgers, fries, milkshakes); leaves a thin frost-film on any glass he holds for more than two minutes.
- Natasha: arrives unannounced through whatever door no one is watching; runs perimeter once before settling; checks the team's mail for tampering without telling anyone she is doing it; leaves without farewells in roughly 80% of departures.
- Blaze: telephones in rather than appears; when present, smokes (Marlboros, observed); does not eat with the others.

**Decision habits at baseline.** Almost no group decisions are made at baseline. The team's calendar is empty by design. When a decision is required (a press request, a public appearance, an invoice), Warren makes it and informs the others, who ratify by silence. This is the team's most consistent decision-architecture: **rule by default through the funder, with passive consent from everyone else.**

**Tells the file would flag.** Warren's flight circuit lengthens when team morale is low (he can be measured against the shoreline). Hercules's wine consumption rises in proportion to Natasha's absence from headquarters — he drinks more when she is not there to be courted or contested. Bobby's joke-rate doubles when Warren is visibly stressed; he is regulating Warren, not himself. Natasha leaves earlier on days Blaze is present, and Blaze stays shorter when she is.

---

## II. LOW-GRADE STRESS (Press, Public Appearances, Bureaucratic Friction)

The Champions are publicly photogenic and privately allergic to the apparatus that makes them so. Press conferences, civic ceremonies, permit hearings — the connective tissue of being a sanctioned super-team in a major American city — produce a characteristic stress signature.

**At a press conference (multiple observed, #4, #11, #15):** Warren takes the lectern. He prepares remarks; he sometimes reads them. Hercules stands stage-right and *projects*, arms folded across the chest in a deliberate sculptural pose he has refined over millennia of being looked at — he is not nervous, he is *posed*. Natasha stands stage-left at a precise three-quarter angle to the cameras, which both photographs well and provides peripheral coverage of the room; she answers questions in the third-shortest sentence that will satisfy them. Bobby fidgets — shifts weight every twelve to fifteen seconds, picks at his cuffs, ices a glass of water on the lectern table without realizing. Blaze, when present, does not speak; when asked direct questions he defers to Warren with a head-tilt.

**Decision habits under low stress.** The team's decisions in this register are *optical*: how will this look, what will the press say, can we be photographed leaving together. Warren is the optical conscience. Natasha quietly vetoes the worst ideas by not participating in them — a tell only the alert observer catches, because she does not announce a veto, she simply is not there. Hercules will agree to almost any photo opportunity and must be steered away from the most undignified ones. Bobby will agree to anything Warren agrees to.

**Friction tells.** When bureaucratic friction rises (permits denied, lawsuits filed, civic complaints lodged), Warren over-functions: longer hours at the office, more flight circuits, sharper grooming. Natasha *under-functions* in a precise way — she will solve a single problem brilliantly and ignore the next four. Hercules will offer to physically intimidate the offending bureaucrat and must be talked down by Warren in low, steady cadence. Bobby will joke about the bureaucrat's appearance. Blaze, telephoned about the matter, will say "do what you think is right" and hang up within ninety seconds.

---

## III. PRE-MISSION (Threat Inbound, Briefing, Suit-Up)

The team's most coherent state. Once a threat is named, the Champions become recognizable to themselves as a unit, and the behavioral signature tightens dramatically within minutes.

**Briefing room behavior.** Warren projects the intelligence (often via Foundation resources or news feed). Natasha asks two to three clarifying questions, all tactical, none editorial. Hercules requests the threat's identity and *lineage* — he wants to know if he has fought it, or its father, before; he is mapping the encounter to mythic precedent, which is both a real strategic asset and a self-soothing ritual. Bobby asks where the fight will happen and whether civilians are present (a real concern, but expressed in joke-form: "Anywhere I can't drop a glacier on?"). Blaze asks the time of day. If it is approaching nightfall he becomes visibly more focused; if it is mid-morning, less so.

**Suit-up sequence.** Iceman ices over in roughly three seconds and tests his coefficient with a quick slide across the room — a tic, every time, even when the room is too small. Angel removes shirt and outer wear with practiced economy (he has done this since adolescence) and rolls his shoulders twice to loosen the wing musculature. Hercules does not change; his costume *is* his clothing, and he treats this as evidence of authenticity. Natasha disappears for forty-five to ninety seconds and returns in costume with her hair recoiled; nobody has ever seen her change and the team has stopped noticing. Blaze, if present in human form, walks outside, mounts the bike, and the transformation occurs en route.

**Decision habits.** Tactical decisions are made fast and well in this window. The decision-axis is functionally **Natasha-proposes, Hercules-amends, Warren-approves, Bobby-and-Blaze-execute.** This is the team's actual command structure and it is never written down. Hercules's amendments are usually about which targets he personally engages (he claims the largest); Warren's approval is usually pro forma but his veto, when issued, holds. Bobby never proposes a plan in this register but executes other people's plans with high fidelity. Blaze proposes nothing and executes asymmetrically — he goes where the violence is densest and trusts the rest of the team to flow around him.

**Tells inbound to combat.** The team becomes physically closer in the minutes before deployment — they cluster in a way they do not cluster at baseline. Natasha's perimeter-checking *stops*; she trusts the in-team window. Hercules laughs more (genuinely, not performatively). Bobby's jokes get sharper and funnier — the nervous-system idle becomes actual wit under load. Warren grows quieter and his shoulders set. Blaze, on the bike, does not look back.

---

## IV. ACTIVE COMBAT / THREAT ENGAGEMENT

The Champions in combat are the Champions at their most defensible, professionally. The behavioral signature here is the team's strongest argument for its own existence.

**Tactical signatures.**
- **Hercules** engages the largest opponent first, by reflex; he will *trade* hits rather than evade them, because his pain economy permits it; he calls his shots aloud in a quasi-Homeric narration that doubles as battlefield communication ("Now feels Hercules' might —!") which teammates have learned to parse as a *location signal* (he is announcing where he is on the battlefield).
- **Black Widow** moves to the high ground or the flank within the first ten seconds; she fights with economy and never throws a punch she could substitute with a Widow's-Bite or a leg-sweep; she communicates in hand signals to Warren overhead and in spoken half-sentences to Hercules at ground level.
- **Angel** takes air, performs reconnaissance, ferries Natasha to position when she signals, extracts wounded civilians; he is the team's mobility layer; his combat output is moderate but his battlefield-awareness contribution is the highest on the team.
- **Iceman** builds infrastructure mid-fight — slides, walls, barriers, the famous ice-bridges — and uses them to position himself and others; he ices in patterns (a tell: he will always build a perimeter before an attack, because he wants the civilians contained, even if no one ordered it).
- **Ghost Rider** functions as area denial. He goes where he is needed by gravitational instinct toward concentrated malice; he uses the hellfire chain as a kinetic tool and the penance stare almost never (it is, in the run, used sparingly and at high cost). Teammates have learned not to be directly behind him.

**Mutual aid behavior — the team's most photogenic virtue.** Logged instances of inter-team rescue in the seventeen-issue run number in the low dozens. Hercules has shielded Natasha with his body twice. Angel has lifted Iceman out of a collapsing structure once and Natasha out of a fall three times. Iceman has built ice-cover for Hercules under Sentinel fire. Blaze has chained-and-yanked Hercules clear of a Pluto-tier attack. Natasha has talked Blaze down from a partial Zarathos episode mid-fight once, using cadence and proximity rather than touch. *This is the team at its best and the only register in which the Champions are clearly themselves.*

**Tells in combat.** Hercules's narration speeds up when he is enjoying himself and slows when he is genuinely concerned; the team can read his emotional state by his iambs. Natasha goes silent when she is improvising and verbal when she is executing a plan — silence is the warning. Bobby's jokes *stop* when he is at the edge of his power-envelope; humor cessation is a medical signal. Warren's wings beat slower when he is fatigued and he will not say so. Blaze's flame intensity rises with the moral weight of the opponent — petty crooks produce a smaller corona than child-endangerers.

**Decision habits in combat.** Real-time decisions are made by whoever has the best vantage. The team has developed, without articulating it, a **distributed-command protocol** where authority devolves to the member with the best information in the moment. This is genuinely sophisticated and is the single most underrated competency of the Champions; it is also unrepeatable outside combat, because the trigger condition (named external threat) cannot be manufactured in the boardroom.

---

## V. MORAL AMBIGUITY MID-MISSION (Rampage Class, Defectors, Bystander Casualties)

The team's catastrophic failure mode. When a mission's clean-threat profile collapses into ambiguity, the distributed-command protocol *breaks* and the team fragments along the moral-epistemology axis catalogued in §3 of the master file.

**Observed sequence (Rampage arc, #5–6, #15–17).**
1. Ambiguity introduced (the bankrupted small businessman framing, the civilian sympathy, the partial legitimacy of the antagonist's grievance).
2. Hercules continues to engage as if the threat profile were unchanged. He has no register for "this enemy may be partly right."
3. Natasha pauses. She is the team's only member with the trained capacity to revise an operation mid-execution; she will, observably, *stop fighting* and reassess.
4. Warren attempts a verbal de-escalation, which is sincere and ineffectual; he speaks in the cadence of a man used to being listened to because he is paying.
5. Bobby looks at Warren, then Natasha, then Hercules, in that order, trying to identify the authority to defer to; finding none, he keeps fighting at low intensity.
6. Blaze, on the rare occasions he is present for this kind of mission, becomes the wildcard — Zarathos has no ambiguity-protocol and the penance stare cannot adjudicate "partly right."

The team has no procedure for recovering from this break. The mission is concluded, usually by force, and the ambiguity is never processed afterward. The *post*-mortem does not happen.

---

## VI. INTIMACY (Within the Team)

Intimacy at the Champions is **combat-intimate, biographically distant.** Members will take damage for each other and will not ask each other about their parents.

**Dyadic patterns logged.**
- **Warren and Bobby:** the closest dyad, inherited from X-Men adolescence. They will sit together without speaking. Bobby will eat Warren's leftover food without asking. Warren will pick something off Bobby's collar — a parental tic he does not perform for anyone else. They share inside jokes the others do not get and do not explain. *This is the team's only real friendship.*
- **Hercules and Natasha:** charged, contested, oscillating. Hercules courts in a register two and a half millennia out of date; Natasha rebuffs with a precision that is itself a form of attention. They flirt in combat (his narration sometimes addresses her directly mid-fight) and avoid each other off-duty. The unresolved erotic-and-authority tension is one of the team's structural loads.
- **Natasha and Warren:** professional respect, light. They are the two members who can have a budget conversation. Neither pretends the others can.
- **Hercules and Bobby:** older-brother-younger-brother in the warm register. Hercules will lift Bobby (literally) into the air to make a point. Bobby will tease Hercules about his Greek pronunciation. This dyad is unexpectedly stable.
- **Blaze and anyone:** weak. Blaze is the team's loosely-attached member; he has functional warmth with Hercules (the only teammate whose physical scale matches Zarathos's intuited weight) and minimal connection with anyone else.

**Tells of intimacy.** Touch occurs only in two registers: combat (rescue, support) and very low-stakes physical comedy (Hercules lifting Bobby, Warren brushing Bobby's collar). There is essentially no on-panel embrace between members not under threat. Eye contact at baseline is shorter than would be expected for a group of five who live and work together. Members do not use each other's first names with the frequency a healthy team would; the proportion of code-name-to-first-name address is roughly 70/30, which is *high* for a team of this duration.

**Decision habits in intimacy.** Intimate-register decisions (where to eat together, whether to attend a teammate's personal event, whether to ask after a teammate's mood) are *not* made collectively. Each member decides individually, and the team's intimacy is therefore episodic and uncoordinated. Warren remembers birthdays. Natasha does not. Hercules will arrive at a teammate's celebration uninvited and with wine. Blaze will not come.

---

## VII. GRIEF

The team has limited on-panel grief in the run — no member dies during *The Champions* #1–17 — but it has *losses*: civilian casualties on missions, the loss of the Coliseum HQ, repeated reputational injuries, and the slow accumulated grief of failing at the "for the common man" mandate.

**Grief signature.** The Champions do not mourn together. After a bad mission (a civilian casualty, a missed save) the team disperses faster than usual. Headquarters empties within an hour. The next time members reconvene, the loss is not discussed; the agenda moves forward.

**Individual grief tells the file would log.**
- Warren grieves financially — he writes a check, he funds a memorial, he donates to a hospital. He converts grief into capital expenditure within forty-eight hours.
- Hercules grieves rhetorically — he composes a brief eulogy aloud, to whoever is present, and then drinks more than usual for one to two days.
- Natasha grieves in motion — she takes a long run or a long drive (the Pacific Coast Highway northbound, observed) and returns without comment.
- Bobby grieves by joking, which intensifies in proportion to the loss, until at the highest grief-load he stops joking entirely and goes quiet for a day. The cessation, again, is the medical signal.
- Blaze grieves by transformation — he becomes Ghost Rider for longer windows in the days after a loss, which the team correctly intuits as self-punishment and incorrectly intuits as none of their business.

**The team-level grief habit:** convert loss to the next mission. The Champions do not have a memorial register; they have a *next-engagement* register.
